Local News

Social Affairs Bureau Emergency Measures for High Rice Prices 116

Request for Reiteration of the Prohibition on Hoarding and Border Closures

Efforts to Reduce Prices by Two Yuan Within Ten Days

Since the Social Affairs Bureau announced yesterday a limit on the highest price of white rice, not to exceed 20 yuan per stone, it has been found that the price in the northern city was still above 20 yuan yesterday. In the northern and southern city, some rice merchants were even seen informing customers to wait and see how the situation develops before shipping rice to Shanghai. Their intentions are clearly malicious. The Social Affairs Bureau has not yet taken any action as of yesterday, because the announcement had just been issued, and merchants and civilians may not yet be fully aware of it. Moreover, price changes in the market cannot happen overnight. Therefore, the Bureau has ordered the Soy and Rice Industry Association, the Jiagutang Public Association, and rice merchants in the north and south to comply, and has also made the punishment measures clear, so as to avoid punishing without prior warning. At the same time, temporary emergency measures have been submitted to the Mayor for approval. The original report and order are recorded as follows:

Report to the Mayor: The report is submitted for review. The rice price in this city has been rising without falling, making it difficult for the people to eat. I have already submitted a request to your Honor to purchase 200,000 bags of foreign rice and to jointly establish a Rice Price Stabilization Committee with local public organizations to handle price stabilization matters for relief. However, on the 26th of this month, the price of special rice in the northern city reached more than 21 yuan per stone. I have observed that the market situation is still continuing to rise. If restrictions are not immediately imposed, I am sincerely afraid that a food panic will occur, affecting local public order. I immediately issued an announcement that the highest price of white rice is temporarily limited to 20 yuan per stone, with corresponding price limits for other varieties. At the same time, I also ordered various rice industry groups to comply, and set a deadline of ten days to find ways to reduce the price by two yuan. If there are any cases of exceeding the deadline, secretly charging premiums, hoarding, or refusing to sell, I will follow the instructions of your Office No. 2560 and No. 2561, and take appropriate action, I humbly submit. I humbly believe that the current rise in rice prices is not entirely due to poor harvests. It is also due to the excessive cold and snow last winter, making it inconvenient to thresh rice. Farmers, seeing the high price of rice, also have the intention of hoarding, preferring to borrow money to pay rent and accumulate grain instead of selling. Rice merchants are taking advantage of the opportunity, and grain hoarding households are colluding to engage in unscrupulous activities, resulting in rice prices rising to more than 21 yuan even before the time when the old crop is exhausted and the new crop is not yet harvested. A low grain price is harmful to farmers, but a high grain price is harmful to the people's food supply. According to the current market price, farmers have already made substantial profits. Rice merchants and grain hoarding households should consider the difficulties of the times and not seek insatiable greed. They must know that hungry people are like tigers. If there is a situation of robbing and seizing food, how can the interests of these merchants and civilians be preserved? Also, considering that Shanghai is a rice sales area, price limits are not a fundamental solution. If only this city limits prices, while the producing areas remain unrestricted, it is not a win-win solution. This Bureau is deliberating on the market situation and considering the food supply of 2.7 million people. I propose that your Honor quickly forward the serious situation of the people's food supply in this city to the Executive Yuan, ordering all provinces and cities to reiterate the strict prohibition of hoarding and border closures. At the same time, I request the Jiangsu Provincial Government to immediately order Changshu and Wuxi counties to limit the highest price of rough rice to 13 yuan per stone (using the Xihu measure as the standard), and to gradually reduce it to 10 yuan per stone within the shortest possible time, with corresponding price reductions for other varieties of rice, so as to benefit the food supply of all people and benefit farmers.

Order to Rice Industry Groups: For the purpose of compliance, it has been found that the price of rice in this city has been rising continuously in recent days. The price of special rice in the northern city has risen to more than 21 yuan per stone in recent days. Such a high price is detrimental to people's livelihood. This Bureau has issued Announcement No. 131, stating that the highest price of white rice is temporarily limited to 20 yuan per stone from this date, with corresponding price limits for other varieties. It is forbidden to exceed the limit, secretly charge premiums, hoard, or refuse to sell. It is hereby ordered that the relevant parties instruct their colleagues to comply. If anyone dares to undermine the price limit, they will be punished in accordance with the provisions of Article 35, Item 13 of Chapter 3 of the Police Offenses Punishment Regulations, with a detention of five days for first-time offenders, with no commutation allowed. Those who re-offend or commit the offense three or more times will be given a suspension or closure penalty in accordance with Item 2 of the same article. As for hoarding and refusing to sell, it will be enforced on their behalf in accordance with Article 2, Item 1 of the Administrative Enforcement Law. A preliminary notice will be given, and then staff will be dispatched with the Public Security Bureau to sell the rice hoarded by the household at market prices. If there is resistance, it can be enforced with force. The matter has been approved by the Mayor. In addition to separate letters, it is also ordered that within ten days of receiving this document, appropriate measures be taken to further reduce the current price limit by two yuan until the normal market is restored. Comply with this order without fail.

Concession Area: The Pharmaceutical Industry Went on Strike Again Yesterday 117

Suspension of the Executive Committee's Exercise of Authority

Establishment of a Relief Association for Unemployed Workers

Management Decides to Apply to the Municipal Government for Arbitration

The pharmaceutical industry resumed work on the 25th after mediation by the Bureau of Social Affairs. *

Details have been recorded in this newspaper. It is learned that because the management hired detectives *

to arrest [workers] and refused to provide relief, the labor side held a citywide membership meeting at the Pharmaceutical Workers' *

Union yesterday morning at 9:00 am. The Shanghai Special *

Municipality Pharmaceutical Workers' Relief Association for Unemployed Workers was established, the Assistance *

Committee for Unemployed Workers was dissolved, and the Executive Committee's exercise of *

authority was temporarily suspended, with full authority transferred to the Relief Association. The concession area continues *

the strike to the end. After the meeting, the group marched to the Municipal Government *

to petition, requesting the Municipal Government to reject the Pharmaceutical Industry Association's application *

for arbitration and order them not to be stubborn. The section chief of the Second Department received *

them and replied that the case would definitely not disadvantage the labor side, and the result was extremely *

satisfactory. If the management refuses to accept again, further *

measures will be considered. The document submitted by the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union to the Municipal Government *

is recorded below:

Submitting [this] as a petition matter: It is noted that the relief issue for unemployed workers in this industry *

has been repeatedly submitted to Party and government organs for review. On March *

7th of this year, relief measures were drafted and submitted to the Citizen Training Committee *

for instructions. The Citizen Training Committee issued Directive No. 2385, *

instructing that negotiations should first be conducted with the Pharmaceutical Industry Association. Later, because the association *

refused to comply with the order, on the 11th of this month, [workers] automatically began implementing relief at the association. * It was unexpected that the management in the concession area would disregard the Party headquarters *

and use the excuse that the government organs had not issued a clear order, hiring a large number of police officers, *

relying on the protection of imperialists, and using force to suppress relieved *

workers, which aroused public anger. On the same day, a resolution was passed at a citywide membership *

meeting that the concession area would unanimously go on strike. The Bureau of Social Affairs convened two *

mediations, but the management was cunning and made excuses to delay. It was not until the third mediation on the 20th of this month *

that representatives were sent to attend, but they were insincere, resulting in no results. The chairman of the committee then *

announced the adjournment of the meeting and scheduled a re-discussion for the 24th. When the deadline arrived, the management *

suddenly evaded again, so the majority of the committee members agreed on a judgment, such as mediation *

No. 400 (omitted). After receiving the instructions from the Bureau of Social Affairs, the affiliated association *

immediately complied with the order. The management changed its strategy of opposing the Party headquarters *

and instead attacked the Bureau of Social Affairs. On the one hand, it oppressed *

the workers who resumed work and the relieved unemployed members of the affiliated association. The Pharmaceutical *

Industry Association hired a large number of Chinese and Western detectives, stationed six at each *

store, refusing to relieve unemployed workers and publishing large advertisements, *

vigorously promoting [their position], making wild statements, slandering superiors, and attempting to confuse *

the public. To achieve their selfish desires, they exhausted every *

possible trick. The various conspiracies are too numerous to recount. It is noted that this *

relief is based on the Premier's Principle of People's Livelihood, which is to accurately investigate the management's *

business development, assess the lack of personnel in each store, maintain the unemployed's *

livelihood, emphasize humanitarianism, and eliminate social ills, in order *

to maintain public order. This was done after repeated consideration by Party and government organs, *

careful observation of the situations of both sides, and then the direction was determined and permission was granted for implementation, which cannot be compared to reckless actions. However, the management did not carefully consider [the situation] and *

dared to openly attack, not only disregarding the law, but also violating public *

opinion, only knowing to enrich themselves, which is extremely wrong. Therefore, the various points presented by the management *

are briefly refuted as follows. According to the management's reasons for non-compliance, the *

first point is that the actual need is not present, and forced relief is being imposed. It is thought that customers often have to wait three or four hours *

to buy [medicine], and there are complaints. Workers feel that the work is busy *

and hate that they do not have enough hands. Therefore, the so-called actual need is not present *

cannot stand. Since [the relief] is based on principle, investigation of facts, and review by Party *

and government organs, how can there be coercion? This should be refuted *

one. Unemployed workers are mostly due to reduced manpower and unwarranted *

dismissals, or the abuse of apprentices who are dismissed after the expiration of their apprenticeship, blaming [them] for *

immature performance. Tracing the source of the crime, the management can easily evade its responsibility, using *

the pretext of social problems, and not knowing the danger they are inviting. This should be refuted *

two. This strike is actually motivated by righteous indignation *

to protect their own position and interests, with the special permission of the Party headquarters. * To say that [the strike] is incited by the unemployed is to blame others *

and not blame themselves, wanting to cover up the entire social scene with one hand, which is too *

unrealistic and exposes their shortcomings. Moreover, the Law on the Handling of Labor Disputes *

only stipulates that strikes or work stoppages are not allowed during the mediation or arbitration period, and there is no explicit provision that strikes are not allowed in all cases when disputes occur. Now, the Pharmaceutical Industry Association wants to *

misrepresent the facts and fabricate charges, and believe that the mediation committee's judgment *

that wages should be paid during the strike period is not appropriate, but [they] do not know that *

Chapter IV, Article 37 allows [the mediation committee] to exercise its authority. This should be refuted *

three. In this case, the Bureau of Social Affairs convened a mediation, but the *

management was absent twice. Although [they] dealt with it perfunctorily the third time, *

[they] were suddenly absent the fourth time, which clearly shows that [they] were insincere. The mediation committee *

made a decision based on the provisions of Chapter III, Section 1, Article 39, *

which is legal. However, the management said that this was a one-sided opinion and made a decision without authorization, unaware of the procedures for handling labor disputes and arbitrarily judging the handling of the mediation committee as inappropriate. This *

should be refuted four. Based on the above four points, the association's application *

for arbitration is completely invalid and should be strictly rejected *

by Your Honor and not accepted. [We] also pray that [Your Honor] orders the association to obey the mediation committee's *

decision and seek a solution as soon as possible. Moreover, most *

of the management are willing to accept, but they are restricted by the authority of one or two manipulators, *

and have to bow their heads and obey orders. The willingness of each store to accept can serve as ironclad proof. Therefore, a special *

report of the entire situation is made, earnestly requesting Your Honor to reject the association's request *

and investigate and deal with the instigators and manipulators, in order to curb the troubles and emphasize *

the people's livelihood, [We] await orders with utmost urgency. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Special *

Municipal Government, Shanghai Special Municipality Pharmaceutical Workers' Union, 19. *

3. 27. There is also an open letter to compatriots and a declaration seeking assistance from all sectors (long, omitted).

It is heard that the management has resolved to apply to the Municipal Government for arbitration in accordance with the law, and decided *

to hold an emergency meeting of all industries at the National Medical and Pharmaceutical Association on March 30th to elect representatives to attend the Municipal Government arbitration, *

and convened the executive committee of the association yesterday to prepare.

Conversation with an Official from the Bureau of Social Affairs: The Pharmaceutical Industry's Case of Employing Unemployed Workers 118

Other Industries Cannot Use This as an Example

Yesterday, an E-Chen Social Affairs reporter spoke with Director Pan about the pharmaceutical industry's strike and market closure *

, which was reported in yesterday's newspaper. As the case was resolved fairly by the Mediation Committee *

, there are reasonable grounds. To understand the contents, [the reporter] again *

inquired in detail from Mr. Guo Yongxi, the chairman of the Mediation Committee of the case. *

According to [Guo], Director Pan instructed [him] to mediate the case of the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union's request *

to hold the management responsible for employing unemployed workers. At first, [Guo] thought that providing relief *

to unemployed workers was a social problem, not an industry or local problem. *

However, China is now suffering from poverty, and the government is also in the same situation. To provide relief *

to the entire unemployment problem, it may be difficult to do so in a short period of time. Therefore, the comrades *

in the Municipal Party Headquarters who were handling this case first investigated the pharmaceutical stores to see if *

there was a need to add people to the work situation, and if there was a *

possibility of adding people in the economic situation, as the basis for handling this case. [Guo] and a comrade *

personally went to Hu Qing Yu Tang, Tong Han Chun, Cai Tong De, and other pharmacies to get medicine, and *

some prescriptions took up to four hours to get. [They] also went to Peng *

Shou Tang, Wang Da Ji, and other pharmacies to get medicine, and some prescriptions took two or three *

hours to get. When [they] asked the workers at the counter, they all said that they were *

too busy. [They] also investigated the business conditions of the pharmacies. According to those familiar with the contents, *

most of the more than 300 pharmacies in Shanghai made money last year, *

only the amount of profit varied. As for the very small pharmacies that *

lost money, it was less than 10 percent. Therefore, it was learned that the pharmacies *

had the possibility of adding people in the economic situation, and there was even more *

of a need to add people in the work situation. Moreover, because the workers were too busy, it was inevitable that they would prescribe the wrong medicine, *

harming the lives of the people. For example, Hu Qing Yu, Ye Tian De, Ren Ren Tang, Han San He, *

and other pharmacies had cases last year where they prescribed the wrong medicine, causing disputes with patients, *

and even lawsuits in court. Therefore, the reason for the decision of this mediation to allow Hu Qing Yu *

and other 53 pharmacies to separately add qualified unemployed workers is *

here. It is in accordance with the central government and the municipal government's intentions that these 53 *

pharmacies (one-sixth of the city) have a need to hire employees and should *

give priority to hiring unemployed workers. If pharmacies *

had no possibility of adding people in the economic situation, and there was no *

need to add people in the work situation, then not only could [the Bureau] not order them to add people, but [the Bureau] could not reject their *

reduction [of staff]. For example, silk factories, cotton weaving factories, cigarette factories, and match factories *

are now successively applying to close down. The Bureau of Social Affairs has not prevented their closure. Each *

of these industries has tens of thousands of unemployed workers, and the Bureau of Social Affairs has not ordered each *

of these industries to separately employ [workers], because these factories not only have no need to add people, *

but also have no possibility of adding people, and when there is no need to add people in the work situation, the Bureau of Social Affairs cannot force them to add people. The reason is that although the work of each industry is busy, it is not related to social security, but the busy work of the pharmaceutical industry is related to *

the lives of the people. Outsiders do not know this and think that the pharmaceutical industry can arrange for unemployed *

workers, and other industries will follow suit. This is because they do not understand the situation, *

resulting in this misunderstanding. Merchants should not worry too much.

Chinese Taxpayers Association Seeks Opinions 120

Fourteen Points to Deal with the Concession Issue

The Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association, having received a letter from Mr. Fei Tang, consultant of the Public Concession *

Bureau, requesting Chinese groups and individuals to express their opinions for the sake of improvement research, believes that this *

matter is of great importance to the immediate rights of the Chinese in the concession. *

Therefore, it has drafted fourteen points and distributed them to various groups, ordering *

each to express their views in writing for the purpose of collecting and forwarding them. *

The points are recorded below: (1) Should the Public Concession be taken back immediately, *

or should a transitional period be set? (2) Before the Public Concession is taken back, the *

management rights of the concession should be gradually transferred to the Chinese? *

(3) Should the budget, final accounts, and general administrative guidelines of the Bureau of Works *

be approved or recognized by the Chinese taxpayers? (4) The Bureau of *

Works has a total of three Chinese directors and nine foreign directors. Now *

it has been decided to add two more Chinese directors, making a total of five. Is this already *

satisfactory? (5) If it is believed that five Chinese directors are not satisfactory, *

then how many should there be in total, the same as the nine foreign directors, *

or should it be based on the proportion of tax revenue, with the Chinese accounting for 55 percent *

and foreigners accounting for 45 percent, making it eleven seats? *

(6) The Western Taxpayers Association usually holds a meeting once a year *

, gathering and dispersing quickly, with little time for discussion. Can this kind of meeting's power to supervise the Bureau of Works *

be considered great? (7) If it is believed that the above-mentioned Western Taxpayers Association meeting does not have much *

power to supervise the Bureau of Works, then representatives (or councilors) should be elected by Chinese and foreign taxpayers *

to form a standing municipal council to supervise the Bureau of Works? *

(8) All the senior officials of the Bureau of Works are foreigners. Is there sufficient distance between the Chinese and the Bureau of Works? *

(9) Are the official documents, gazettes, and annual reports of the Bureau of Works all in *

English, making it inconvenient for the Chinese? (10) Regarding the above two items, *

if there is distance or inconvenience, then employing Chinese as senior officials in the Bureau of Works *

and using both Chinese and English for official documents, gazettes, and annual reports can eliminate distance or inconvenience? (11) Do the *

public officials in various departments of the Bureau of Works deliberately nitpick and make things difficult when Chinese people request to handle *

matters, demanding bribes? Do [they] take advantage of crises to encroach on or defraud Chinese property? *

If there are facts, can they be recorded? (12) Are the Chinese schools *

of the Bureau of Works too few? Should Chinese schools be run by the Chinese? *

(13) Does the Bureau of Works believe that the hygiene facilities for the Chinese, *

such as hospitals, are too incomplete? (14) Should the household registration in the concession *

be investigated? In addition, if there are other opinions, please indicate them.

Representatives of Huai Bei Salt Affairs and River Transportation Arrive in Shanghai 123

Requesting Equal Treatment for Salt Catty from the Ministry of Finance

Xiba in Huaibei is the hub for transporting salt into Anhui and Henan. Recently, due to the increase in sea *

transportation, each bag of salt catty for sea transportation is 109 catties, while river *

transportation is still 105 catties, and is also affected by the unequal salt catty *

, resulting in stagnation. Tens of thousands of laborers who depend on salt for their livelihood are even more *

impoverished. Now, river transport merchants have sent Li Wenbing, Zhou Gongwang, *

and Wang Yaozong to Shanghai to request *

equal treatment from the Audit Office of the Salt Affairs Department of the Ministry of Finance. It is heard that Minister Song and Director Zou have *

agreed in principle to uphold justice and equal treatment. The representatives will report to the merchants for tax payment and transportation soon.

encountered a bandit alert at Majiazai immediately after resuming navigation on the Yichang-Hankou route on March 8th. *

number of passengers traveling east from Hankou to Shanghai on various Chinese and foreign steamers on the Yangtze River has suddenly increased, especially *

third-class and steerage passengers. Recently, 31 British, *

Japanese, and Chinese steamers have been sailing on the Yangtze River route, with an average of more than three *

thousand people arriving in Shanghai every day, mostly from Hubei Province.

Nanyang Prohibits Private Bureau Packages 125

Sent Before May 1st

Not Treated as Underpaid Mail

The British-owned Kuala Lumpur Post Office previously sent a letter to China, along with a notice from the *

governments of the Nanyang Islands and the Malay Peninsula, stating that *

from March 31st onwards, all postage fees must be charged at *

the full rate according to the Postal Union rate. It is heard that the Chinese Post Office *

, due to the British Post Office's urgent deadline, is deeply concerned that the total packages *

sent by its national private bureaus from China to Nanyang will be subject to *

charges for underpayment because they have not yet paid the full fee. The Chinese Post Office immediately sent a telegram *

requesting that the full charge be extended to May 1st. *

The incoming and outgoing telegrams are translated below: (1) Translation of the March *

25th telegram from the Chinese Post Office to the British-owned Kuala Lumpur Post Office: Regarding your postal service's March 5th letter regarding the new *

private bureau system implemented from April 1st, the matter was unexpected. *

This postal service is unable to fully prepare, and for letters in private bureau *

packages, cannot implement the full Postal Union rate from that day as your postal service does. *

However, from May 1st, the Postal Union fee is expected to be implemented. *

Until that day, please do not treat letters in private bureau packages sent from *

China that are paid according to the usual reduced rate as underpaid mail. *

Please reply by telegram if this is feasible. (2) Translation of the British-owned Kuala Lumpur Post Office's telegram on March *

26th: Your esteemed telegram of the 25th is noted with respect. Before May 1st, the *

private bureau package letters sent from China that are paid according to the usual reduced rate *

will not be treated as underpaid mail here. However, total package letters sent from here *

must be paid at the full international postage rate from March 31st onwards.

Record of the Shanghai County Defense Meeting 127

More Than Twenty Representatives Arrived Yesterday

The Shanghai County Government held a defense meeting in the county government hall at 2:00 PM yesterday, with more than twenty people in attendance. The meeting was presided over by County Magistrate Leng Jun. After the opening ceremony, the *

chairman first reported the origins of convening the defense meeting, and then began the discussion, which lasted until 6:00 PM. The *

attendees and resolutions are recorded below:

Attendees: The attendees at yesterday's meeting included *

County Magistrate Leng Jun, Wu Jingqing, Liu Rentao, and Lü Zhe of the County Party Headquarters, *

Cai Zhongji of the Public Security Bureau, Shen Chunlin, director of the First Branch of the Public Security Bureau, Fan Qinlie, director of the Second *

Branch, Chen Zijin, director of the Third Branch, Cheng Zhichao, director of the Fourth Branch, *

Yang Fulin, director of the Third District, Ren Yongkang, director of the Fifth District, *

Bi Huan, director of the Fourth District, Zhao Zhibai, director of the Fourth District Security Corps, Wang Chengyao, *

director of the Sixth District Branch Corps, and more than twenty others.

Resolutions: The defense measures resolved are as follows: (1) *

Establish Temporary Observation Posts: Public Security Branches in each district, which usually focus *

on the patrol system, should, in this time of tight defense, establish several *

observation posts at important traffic points in the towns and villages where no posts have been established, to maintain order. (2) Inspect Lodgings, *

Teahouses, and Amusement Venues: Each Public Security Branch and Security Corps should send several *

patrol officers to jointly inspect lodgings, teahouses, and *

amusement venues daily to check for bandits and reactionary elements lurking. *

If there are people of unknown origin, they should be taken back to the branch for questioning. If *

necessary, an inspection station may be established to inspect passengers getting on and off ships, trains, and *

cars. (3) Joint Patrols: Each Public Security Branch and Security Corps should send several patrol officers and corps soldiers, formed into patrol *

teams, to set off together, day and night, to patrol the towns and villages in their jurisdiction, *

as well as remote areas. The patrol routes should be temporarily determined by the district director *

and branch director. (4) Assist in Case of Alarm: In case of bandit alarm in each village, the local police corps should immediately join forces to suppress [the bandits] and *

notify neighboring districts to block [them] to prevent escape. If there are many bandits, *

they may request assistance from the stationed water police and anti-smuggling camp soldiers, as well as neighboring police *

corps. At the same time, a telegram should be sent to the county bureau to request that the garrison commander send *

troops to suppress [the bandits]. Those captured by the Public Security Branch should be *

sent to the County Public Security Bureau, and those captured by the district Security Corps should be sent *

to the County Security Corps Office for investigation and reporting. (5) Joint Rendezvous: Patrol police officers of each branch Security Corps should rendezvous with the police *

corps of neighboring districts once every three days, and rendezvous with neighboring counties once every ten days on the fifth day of the month. *

They must exchange rendezvous credentials. (6) Reports: The branch directors and district corps *

directors should report the defense matters handled, and in addition to reporting special incidents at any time, *

they should each report to the county government Public Security Bureau once every five days and attach the exchanged rendezvous credentials. The reporting format will be determined separately. (7) Investigation: The *

district police corps should investigate whether the defense arrangements are appropriate and whether the staff are *

actually implementing them. The director of the County Public Security Bureau should go to each district to conduct strict *

investigations from time to time, provide guidance, and report the investigation results *

to the county magistrate for review. (8) Firearms and Ammunition: The firearms and ammunition of each Public Security Branch are insufficient *

, and the county will request the Songhu Garrison Command and the Civil Affairs Department to allocate *

them to strengthen their strength. (9) Police Salaries: The police salaries of each Public Security Branch are in arrears, and the county government will borrow some money, and the district directors will try their best *

to borrow from the local area. After the discussion, it was 6:00 PM, and the meeting adjourned.

Japanese Torpedo Squadron to Arrive in Shanghai 130

The torpedo squadron of the First Fleet of the Japanese Navy, led by Rear Admiral Goto Akira, commanding the torpedo ships Naka, and destroyers No. 15, 67, and the 27th Squadron's Wakatake, Sasae, Hayae, Ogi, Fuji, Usu, Tsuta, Ashi, Hishi, [missing character], and Fuyo, Karukaya, Yugao, and Asagao, a total of sixteen ships, are coming to Shanghai from Sasebo. This has already been reported in this newspaper. We now understand that the squadron's warships departed from Japan yesterday, crossed the Yellow Sea to Shanghai, and are scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on the morning of the 30th. There are over 190 warrant officers and over 900 petty officers on board each ship. Upon arrival in Shanghai, Japanese officials and civilians in this port have agreed to welcome them at the pier and have decided on the squadron's itinerary after arriving in Shanghai as follows: On the 30th at 4:00 PM, Japanese officials in Shanghai will hold a welcome reception at the New Public Gardens. At 6:30 PM, naval officers from the Shanghai First Overseas Dispatch Unit will host a banquet for the captains of each ship at the Japanese Club. At noon on the 31st, Rear Admiral Goto will host a banquet on the Naka for the officials as a return gesture. At 6:30 PM in the evening, the Japanese residents of Shanghai will host a banquet for the squadron's officers at the Japanese Club. On this day, the warrant officers of each ship will go ashore for sightseeing. On April 1st at 8:00 AM, the petty officers will disembark at the Customs Wharf and go to Gujiawan to pay respects at the naval cemetery. That evening, the acting Minister Chong Guangkui will host a banquet for the officers of each ship. On the afternoon of April 2nd at 4:00 PM, the squadron's ships, led by Rear Admiral Goto, will leave Shanghai and head to Dalian and other places, it is said.

Japanese Aircraft to Suspend Flights After Trial Period 131

Ninth Flight Today

The Sino-Japanese Liaison Aviation flight, which was previously approved by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for four trial flights, has now completed its trial period. It is now scheduled to fly from Fukuoka to Shanghai for the fourth time today, and return to Fukuoka the next day, temporarily suspending flights in accordance with the agreement. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Negotiates with Mitsui 132

Regarding the Collision of the "Gongping" Steamer

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Gongping" steamer was damaged by the Japanese steamer "Daishu Maru" in Zhenjiang last month. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company negotiated with Mitsui & Co., the manager in Shanghai, requesting compensation for the damage. The Japanese company ordered the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to send representatives to Japan for negotiations, which the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company refused. Subsequently, Mitsui sent a representative, Mr. Okubo, from Shanghai to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company for negotiations. The Japanese representative proposed the following solutions: (1) Each party would be responsible for the damage to their own ship; (2) The Chinese ship would be tried by the Chinese Maritime Court, and the Japanese ship would be tried by the Japanese Maritime Court, and the consular office would be notified. Yesterday, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company rejected the proposal, arguing that since the "Gongping" was hit by the Japanese ship, the responsibility lay with the "Daishu Maru," and the Japanese company should bear full responsibility and be subject to trial by the Chinese Maritime Court. It also stated that the matter should be resolved quickly without delay. This intention has been communicated to Mitsui & Co. in a letter.

Local News II

Zhao Tieqiao Newly Appointed Manager of Jiyu Company Sues Li Guojie Again 138

Did the Plaintiff Have the Intention to Sue?

Raising the Issue of the Subject of the Lawsuit

The Court Believed No Debate Was Necessary

The Plaintiff Should Appear in Court to Provide Evidence

Zhao Tieqiao Dismissed Li Guojie from His Post, Zhaoshangju General *

The mutual lawsuits between Zhao Tieqiao, the Director-General of the China Merchants Bureau, and Li Guojie, the manager of Jiyu Company, *

have already been reported in this newspaper. Now, Zhao Tieqiao states that Li was appointed as the manager of Jiyu *

Company by himself. Recently, he suddenly dismissed Li from this position *

and appointed the company's deputy manager, Fu Jucun, to the position, leaving a vacancy for deputy *

manager, which was filled by another staff member, Mr. Li. After the announcement, *

Li Guojie did not comply with the order to hand over the position. Fu then hired a lawyer to sue Li in the Provisional *

Court for refusing to hand over the position.

Raising the Issue of the Subject of the Lawsuit　　Yesterday afternoon *

at two o'clock, Judge Feng Shide specially opened the Tenth Court to summon *

both parties. Neither party appeared in court in person, and each was represented by a lawyer. *

Defendant's lawyer, Li Cishan, stated that plaintiff Fu Jucun had *

expressed to others that he had no intention of suing, thus raising the issue of the subject of the lawsuit. *

Plaintiff's lawyer, Qin Liankui, debated with him. Judge Feng *

believed that on this point, the plaintiff should appear in court to provide evidence, and there was no *

need for further debate. He also ordered the plaintiff's lawyer to state the *

facts of the lawsuit.

China Merchants Bureau and Jiyu Company　　Lawyer Qin *

began by stating that the case was a dispute between the current manager and the former manager. *

The current manager, Fu Jucun, was appointed by Zhao Tieqiao, the Director-General of the China Merchants *

Bureau, who was acting as the special commissioner. As for the name of Jiyu Company, *

it was first discovered in the third year of the Republic of China. At that time, the bureau's *

assets were being mortgaged for foreign debt, so Jiyu Company was established *

to try to remedy the situation. The stamp on the Jiyu stock *

clearly shows the relationship between the company and the China Merchants Bureau, and the *

office staff within the company are also concurrently serving as staff of the China Merchants Bureau.

Letter of Appointment of Jiyu Manager　　Until the *

sixteenth year of the Republic of China, the National Government, in view of the fact that the China Merchants Bureau was controlled by political *

criminals and corrupt merchants and the bureau's affairs were corrupt, specially appointed commissioners such as Zhang Renjie *

to reorganize it. Thus, the Supervision Office was successively established, and then the *

General Management Office was established. At that time, the former directors of the bureau had been investigated and *

dealt with. Supervisor Wang then appointed Li Guojie to act on behalf of the board of directors *

and also appointed him as the manager of Jiyu Company. Director-General Zhao also appointed *

him. The letter of appointment from Zhao appointing Li as the manager of Jiyu Company was kept *

on file and presented as evidence. The date of appointment was March 13th of the seventeenth *

year. Defendant's lawyer, Li Cishan, immediately stood up and stated that the *

defendant absolutely denied being appointed to act on behalf of the board of directors and as manager, *

both matters.

Who Drafted the Two Sets of Rules?　　Lawyer Qin continued *

that there were also two sets of rules that could prove that Jiyu *

Company was an affiliated organization of the China Merchants Bureau. The rules were drafted in the seventeenth *

year. One was the Provisional Rules of the China Merchants Bureau. Article 14, paragraph 8, and the proviso of Article 1, paragraph 2, of the rules *

contained clear provisions. The other was the Rules of Jiyu Company, which *

stated in Article 2 that the company shall have one manager and one deputy manager, appointed by the *

General Management Office and subject to the supervision and control of the Management Office. *

These rules were drafted by the defendant himself and submitted to the General Management *

Office to be forwarded to the Supervisor for record. Upon hearing this, the defendant's lawyer *

stood up again and stated that the rules were drafted by Zhao. If it was believed that the defendant drafted them, evidence should be presented to prove it.

Jiyu is a Subsidiary of the China Merchants Bureau　　Plaintiff's lawyer *

continued by stating that since the defendant was the manager appointed by the Director-General of the China Merchants Bureau, *

which had been proven, then the Director-General naturally had the power to dismiss him. *

The Central Government ordered Minister Wang to supervise the reorganization, and Zhao was acting as the special commissioner. *

Zhao should comply with the order to take over the position. Unexpectedly, the defendant said that he would not hand over the position no matter *

what, or send telegrams, or publish in newspapers, hoping to gain sympathy through words. *

Now, even the rules he drafted and the letter of appointment he accepted were denied. *

However, the plaintiff still had evidence that could prove that Jiyu was indeed an affiliated *

organization of the China Merchants Bureau. That evidence was the defendant's submission to the municipal government to register Jiyu. *

The document clearly stated that the articles of association of Jiyu Company could not be separated from the articles of *

association of the China Merchants Bureau and exist independently. Therefore, the articles of association were actually a supplementary set of articles of association to the China Merchants Bureau. If Jiyu wanted to independently *

draft articles of association, it would require a resolution by all the shareholders of the China Merchants Bureau. From this, it could be known that Jiyu was a subsidiary of the China Merchants Bureau.

The Defendant Lawyer's Indignant Words　　The defendant's lawyer *

interjected and said that the plaintiff and Zhao Tieqiao were not shareholders of the China Merchants Bureau or Jiyu. *

Their actions were no different from seizing the property of merchants and civilians. What about the dignity of the country? *

He spoke with an expression of indignation.

Party and National Laws Should Be Bound　　The plaintiff's lawyer *

then stated that the plaintiff was appointed by Zhao, and Zhao's acting as the reorganization commissioner *

was granted by the Central Government. Those under the Party rule should naturally be bound by all Party *

and national laws. Although Li Guojie had a special *

status, he should still obey the Party and the country. Zhao Tieqiao did not dismiss and replace staff in his *

private capacity, but according to his authority, he could indeed replace them. *

Now, it only needs to be studied whether the company is an affiliated product of the China Merchants Bureau. *

If it is indeed subordinate to the China Merchants Bureau, then it cannot be said to be seizure.

The Proposition of Subsidiary Saving the Main Business　　The investigation of the China Merchants Bureau *

borrowing money from foreign countries and mortgaging its property was not done in the name of the company. *

Its assets and money were stipulated in the articles of association to be handed over to the *

General Management Office. When the government appointed Zhang Renjie and others to reorganize, the defendant *

expressed his opinion in the meeting, also saying that the company was a subsidiary of the China *

Merchants Bureau and advocating that the subsidiary save the main business. Upon hearing this, the defendant's *

lawyer immediately stood up and argued that at that time, the defendant believed that the members of the Cleaning Committee were all fair and honest, so he had this proposition. *

As for Zhao Tieqiao, he was of inferior character, and the government also criticized his *

measures as being unorthodox. If the government were to replace him with someone else, the defendant would still have the intention to discuss it.

If Appointed Before, Can Be Dismissed Later　　The plaintiff's lawyer *

continued by saying that the government's management of the bureau originally intended to reorganize it. *

If the bureau and the company were separated, then the bureau would be in even more danger. *

The superior land properties are all in the hands of the company. If the defendant is allowed to refuse to hand over the position, *

how can it be reorganized? If the defendant's proposition is followed, it will inevitably lead to unimaginable consequences. *

The price of the bureau's stock has already fallen. If the defendant's proposition is followed, the bureau will go bankrupt. Let *

it go bankrupt, and the company will become wealthy. Only the stock, *

the bureau and the company cannot be separated, as has been stated before, and it will inevitably become half useful and half useless. *

Zhao was ordered by the National Government and had no choice but to commission someone to take over the company *

so that it could be reorganized together with the China Merchants Bureau, in order to fulfill the intention of the National Government's commission. *

Since Li was appointed as the manager before, he can be dismissed later, and so on.

The Signature on the Stub of the Letter of Appointment　　The defendant's lawyer *

then requested a postponement, as the response time would be very long and could not be completed today. *

The court granted his request and instructed them to set a date and summon both parties *

to the court for further questioning, and to return the various documents and evidence submitted by the plaintiff *

to the plaintiff's lawyer for safekeeping, ordering them to be numbered and presented for *

verification next time. The defendant's lawyer was still very suspicious about the stub of the letter of appointment *

appointing Li as the manager of Jiyu, and requested to see it from the other party. *

After the plaintiff's lawyer handed it over for inspection, he unexpectedly wanted to examine it again and requested the court *

to keep the evidence on file or sign it as a mark. Judge Feng *

then signed the evidence before stopping.

Bandit Gang Kidnaps Child, Fails, and Kills One Person with Gunfire 139

Yellow Package Car Company Coveted by Thieves

Child Cries, Thief Abducts on Impulse

Rickshaw Puller Bravely Recovers Child, Captures One Thief

Neighbors Cry "Thief!", End Up Dying a Tragic Death

At 8:50 PM the night before, a dramatic robbery and attempted kidnapping suddenly occurred at the south end of Tangjiawan Small Vegetable *

Market in Ximen, Nanshi. A *

neighbor, Zhang Rutong, was shot and killed, and a thief was captured on the spot by a rickshaw *

puller. The detailed account is recorded below:

Thieves Arrive　　Ren Ruqi, from Funing, Jiangbei, *

is 68 years old and has been running a yellow package car company at No. 1 Dongsheng *

Lane, south of Tangjiawan Small Vegetable Market. He has accumulated some savings, which has made him a target *

for bandits. At 8:50 PM the night before, Ren's family had just finished dinner, and everyone was chatting when suddenly a gang of dramatic thieves *

arrived. Three thieves entered, and the rest kept watch outside, all speaking with a Jiangbei *

accent, each carrying a pistol or Mauser, threatening them to remain silent.

Planning to Kidnap Child　　Ren's family, seeing the situation, all looked at each *

other, listening to them search. The three thieves were about to check the back of the house *

when they saw that the electric light was dim, so they asked the owner for matches. In the light, *

the house was empty. At the same time, people outside were shouting "Thief!" *

The door was wide open because it was not yet late, and the situation had been noticed outside. The thieves knew things were bad and wanted to turn around *

and escape. At that moment, Ren's seven-year-old grandson, named Sanzhangzi, was frightened and cried. *

One thief impulsively grabbed him and held him in his arms, planning to kidnap him and leave.

Neighbor Killed　　Ren opened a yellow package car company, *

so there were many rickshaw pullers at his home. Seeing their young master fall into the hands of the bandits, *

they risked their lives to step forward, snatched the child back, and captured one thief, *

seizing a Mauser pistol No. 710235 and nineteen bullets. *

When there was a lot of noise outside the door, Ren's neighbor across the street, Zhang Rutong (61 years old, also from Funing, making a living selling salted eggs in the *

small vegetable market), suspected it was a fire and rushed out to check. *

When he learned that his neighbor was being robbed, he shouted for help, *

but he was seen by a thief keeping watch at the entrance of Ren's house, who shot him. *

The bullet hit a vital part of his left abdomen, and he immediately fell to the ground and died.

Pursuit Everywhere　　When the incident occurred, cries and police whistles *

sounded everywhere. The Third Squad of the Second Troop of the Police Corps nearby *

and the Second District Headquarters all heard the alarm and dispatched police to pursue the bandits. *

The bandits had already fled far away. Wang, the District Chief of the Second District, immediately went to the victim's *

house to inspect the scene, and then took the captured thief to the headquarters, questioning him *

under strict interrogation. According to the thief, his name was Yin Xiachun, from Jiangbei, 27 years old. *

His confession was unusually cunning, so he ordered the victim to identify him clearly. The *

bandit still denied everything. After taking the confession, Director Wang immediately *

telegraphed the Director of the Bureau and detained the bandit.

Examining the Corpse　　Yesterday morning, the Second District Headquarters ordered *

Dong Zhaotang, the chief of the Thirteenth Tu of the Twenty-fifth Bao, to petition the local *

court for an examination. Around 3 PM, Prosecutor Zhu, *

accompanied by Secretary Yu and Forensic Examiner Xuan, arrived at the scene to verify the body. *

It was verified that he had died from a gunshot wound, and his family was ordered to collect the body and prepare it for burial, awaiting the arrest of the murderer. *

The captured thief was also officially sent to the Justice Department of the General Bureau yesterday *

for interrogation. It was also heard that Director Wang of the Second District was planning to petition the Director of the Bureau *

for Zhang Rutong, who had died, to be given a pension in accordance with the precedent of people helping to capture thieves and being killed, in order to encourage bravery.

Supplementary Record of Robbery Case in Songjiatan, West Shanghai 140

Over a thousand yuan worth of clothing and jewelry stolen

Pawned clothing reveals clues

The head thief captured in Big Sister Mao's room

Four more people captured, totaling seven robbers

Song Gao's house, a farmer in Songjiatan, Chenjiadu, north of Zhoujiaqiao Creek, West Shanghai, *

was suddenly invaded by eight or nine bandits on the night of the 20th of this month at 11 PM. *

Gold jewelry, cash, and clothing were stolen, totaling approximately over one thousand yuan in losses. *

The robbery and the details of the capture of the robbers are recorded in detail below:

Robbery　　Song Gao has a son who recently married a wife, *

just over ten days ago. That night, eight or nine bandits suddenly arrived, first scaling the bamboo fence *

and then prying open the windows, jumping in one after another, each holding a handgun, *

threatening them to remain silent. Two thieves kept watch outside, while the rest rummaged through chests and *

boxes, searching for gold jewelry, clothing, etc. (lasting about two hours), *

packing them into four large bundles, and then they fled with the loot, shouting. The thieves were all wearing *

short clothes and speaking with a Jiangbei accent.

Report　　After being robbed that night, they immediately checked the *

stolen items. The next day, Song Gao opened a list and reported it to the Sixth *

District Police Station, listing the stolen items as one gold bracelet, weighing about one tael, *

one gold ring, four gold buttons, two pairs of gold filigree earrings, *

one gold chain, one clock, one large mirror, four umbrellas, *

two large British woolen hats, two women's leather coats, one women's leather tunic, *

seven bolts of old cloth, over one hundred pieces of men's and women's single-layered and lined clothing, *

one pair of leather shoes, and eighteen yuan in cash, totaling approximately over one thousand yuan in value. *

Upon receiving the report, Section Chief Duan immediately ordered the district's detectives to *

quickly pursue and arrest the robbers and recover the stolen goods, and to solve the case quickly.

Investigation　　The squad leader of the district's detective team, Liu Shaoqing, and *

detectives Gan Youxin and Zhu Fengshan, and others, upon receiving the order, immediately *

went to the victim's house to conduct an on-site investigation, and after inquiring in detail about the appearance of the robbers and *

the robbery situation, they immediately began investigating, going to the nearby *

pawnshops to inquire and wait in ambush. At 7 PM on the 21st, *

the detectives were investigating around Robison Road when they suddenly saw *

that in the Houyu Pawnshop, within about an hour, someone had brought a large *

quantity of clothing and pawned it twice in a row, looking flustered and suspicious. *

They secretly followed him and saw him enter the Zhoujiaqiao *

area's public bathhouse. After inquiring nearby, they learned that the man's surname was Zhu. *

They immediately took the victim to the pawnshop to identify the pawned clothing, *

which was confirmed to be the stolen items. This confirmed that the man was indeed one of the robbers.

Solving the Case　　On the 22nd, the detectives disguised themselves and went *

to the Zhoujiaqiao public bathhouse to inquire if Zhu was there, saying that he had *

a friend who was looking for him. The bathhouse attendant said that Zhu was currently in Big Sister Mao's room at the Hong Kong Hotel on *

Avenue Edward VII in Shanghai. The detectives immediately went to the hotel to secretly investigate, *

confirming that Big Sister Mao was indeed living in room 316. They immediately *

coordinated with the French Concession police to send detectives to arrest the bandit Zhu Jun, *

take him back to the French Concession police station for interrogation, and then take him back to the Sixth District for temporary detention.

Further Arrests　　According to bandit Zhu Jun, there were a *

total of seven people who went to commit the robbery, and after providing their names and *

addresses, squad leader Liu Shaoqing, along with detectives Gan Youxin, Zhu Fengshan, *

Dai Qingyuan, Zhong Juxian, and others, went to various locations to arrest *

the bandits Gao Hanqing, Wang Jinbao, Gu Yizhen, and Jiang Haiqing, as well as *

a suspect named Qian Zhaofu, all of whom were taken back to the Sixth District. *

The two handguns had been taken away by the escaped thieves.

Confessions　　The ringleader of the bandits, Zhu Jun, confessed that he was 44 *

years old, from Tongzhou, and lived in the Zhoujiaqiao public bathhouse. That night, *

he and Wang Jinbao and others went to Songjiatan to commit the robbery. He took a handgun and *

kept watch outside. After using the handgun, he gave it to Wang Liansheng at the public bathhouse. *

There were nine bullets. A total of seven people went. After the stolen goods were pawned, *

he used ten yuan, and he was the one who pawned the clothing. In February of this year, *

he had organized a gang of thirteen people to commit a robbery at a certain family on Daxi Road. *

He received three yuan and five cents. Also, on December 27 of last year, *

Lake Bandits Raided Zhangpuzhen 141

Over Fifty Men, Women, Children Kidnapped

Zhangpuzhen, in Kunshan County, Jiangsu Province, *

is the second-largest town in Kunshan County, twelve li away from Kunshan. *

There are hundreds of large and small shops and five or six hundred households in the town, *

protected by a public security branch and water police patrol boats. *

On the morning of the 24th of this month, a large gang of lake bandits suddenly arrived by boat, *

each carrying Mausers and rapid-firing guns. They first raided the public security branch, then raided wealthy households and *

shops, robbing them house by house, with no one spared, and the losses were enormous. After the lake bandits *

robbed the town, they also kidnapped over fifty men, women, and children from the town before leaving.

The Nanking Road Municipal Council to Move 143

According to the Municipal Council Gazette, the Nanking Road Municipal Council and the market behind it,

sold to Silas Aaron Hardoon for 1.3 million taels since November of the year before last,

are now scheduled to be handed over on May 26 of this year. Therefore, once the Western taxpayer annual meeting is held on April 16,

the furniture and belongings therein will be moved. According to the plans for the construction of the hall, it began in 1888,

but due to the difficulty in raising funds, it was not implemented for a long time. In 1897, it was decided

to build the market and the drill hall, which are the buildings of today's Municipal Council,

and it was completed in 1898. Subsequently, the drill hall was opened, also serving as a

place for public gatherings and holding concerts and dances, and renamed the

Municipal Council. For more than 30 years, it has often been a gathering place for the foreign community. Currently, the attached library

will be moved to the old Carlton Hotel, while the market

will be moved to the intersection of Zhejiang Road and Fuzhou Road, where a three-story

market is currently under construction, and will be equipped with elevators and cold storage rooms, it is said.

A Plowing Cattle Competition to be Held in Zhuanqiao 144

Initiated by the County Farmers' Education Center

The Shanghai County Farmers' Education Center, in order to promote the advancement of plowing cattle,

has decided to hold a competition in Zhuanqiao on April 10. Yesterday, special

letters were sent to various organizations to solicit prizes. The original letter and competition

rules are recorded below. The letter states: "Respected Sir/Madam, for the sake of improving

plowing cattle, our center has decided to hold a plowing cattle

competition on April 10. A committee has been organized to prepare for the event. On March 11,

the first committee meeting was held at 1:00 PM, and it was resolved

to solicit prizes from various organizations and groups. We have always admired your concern

for agriculture, and we respectfully request that you grant prizes to encourage participation. We also invite you to come and provide guidance at the time.

We are deeply grateful." The rules are as follows: "Article

1: The purpose of this competition is to promote the advancement of plowing cattle, and it is named

the Shanghai County Farmers' Education Center First Plowing Cattle Competition.

Article 2: During the competition, all plowing cattle may

participate, and their owners will be members of this competition. Article 3: The competition

venue will be located at the Farmers' Education Center. Article 4: The competition

will last for one day, and the date will be determined by the Plowing Cattle Competition Committee.

However, the date may be extended by one day if necessary. Article 5: The staff of this competition will be divided into two departments: administrative and judging.

The detailed rules for their duties will be determined separately. Article 6: The plowing cattle competition will be divided

into three categories: nature, physique, and build. The forms for these categories will be determined separately.

Article 7: Winning members will be given prizes by this competition

to encourage them. Article 8: Prizes for this competition may be

solicited from various organizations. Article 9: The expenses of this competition will be

borne by the Shanghai Farmers' Education Center. Article 10: These rules will be

approved by the Plowing Cattle Competition Committee and submitted to the County Education Bureau for approval and implementation."

The Bao Ming Electric Company Further Reduces Electricity Prices 146

Price Changed to 2.1 Cents Per Unit

To be Implemented Starting March This Year

The Bao Ming Electric Company is small in scale, and its electricity generation costs are relatively high.

Its electricity price was originally set at 2.5 cents per unit. In May of last

year, it was believed that the electricity business must have low prices and be convenient for users

in order to have hope for development. Therefore, starting in June, the price was changed to

2.3 cents per unit. Later, the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau revised the business regulations of the various

electric companies in the city, and all original connection fees were

cancelled. The minimum amount of electricity used was further reduced. The company

complied with these changes one by one, and they were implemented starting in January of this year. Due to the above

fee reductions, the company's total revenue decreased by no less than

4,500 yuan for the entire year. Given its business situation, it was quite

difficult to reduce prices further. Recently, due to continuous requests

from users, the company decided to reluctantly reduce the price of electricity for lighting

and electric fans by another 2 cents per unit, starting in July of this year, i.e., to actually charge 2.

1 cents per unit, and reported this to the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau for record. However, the Bureau believed that the implementation

date was still too late and ordered that it be considered for advancement. It is now known that the

company has complied with the order to advance the implementation to March and has submitted

it for approval on record.

A Cloth Boat Sunk by a Gasoline Boat 147

Shop Assistant and Boatman Killed

The Ren Da Long native cloth store dispatched shop assistant Shen Xingxiang and others to set up branches in Chuansha,

Pudong. The day before yesterday, the branch collected more than 600 pieces of cloth.

The day before yesterday, they hired the boat of Ding He Shang to transport the goods to Shanghai. In the evening, while sailing in Chenjiaxing,

the Ding boat was suddenly violently struck amidships by a gasoline boat heading out of Shanghai.

The boat was split into two pieces. The shipping assistant Wang Baosheng and Ding He Shang, along with

three other boatmen, all fell into the water. Another boatman named Aqi

is missing. The boat sank. Because it was nighttime, rescue was

difficult. It was not until yesterday morning that Ding hired a boat to report the incident to Shanghai. On the one hand, people were sent to

guard the area. The store hired a boat to salvage the sunken cargo.

Only dozens of bolts of native cloth were salvaged. The remaining goods were swept away by the tide. As for

the shipping assistant Wang Baosheng and the boatman Aqi, their bodies have not yet

been recovered.

A Record of a Couple Eloping with a Child 149

Shao Xishi is extremely bored

Qian Gong's Past is Now Wrong

Qian Sanguan's wife, Gong, a villager from Xiaoqiaotou Township near Yangshuyuan, Wuxi,

is 38 years old this year. Her husband passed away seven years ago, leaving

two daughters and one son. The eldest daughter is named Afeng, and is 14 years old this year.

The second daughter, Lingdi, is 11 years old this year. The youngest son is named Lingbao. Her husband

died when she was still pregnant with him, and he is now seven years old. Although the family has a small amount of land,

two to three mu, no one has cultivated it since her husband died, resulting in a lack of support for the four members of the family.

Therefore, the year after her husband's death, Gong became involved with the tailor Shao Xishi.

Since they could not be open about it in the countryside,

Page 16

that winter, she took her children to Shanghai under the pretext of working.

She came to Shanghai with her lover and rented a room upstairs at Yinha Li, Minguo Road.

However, Shao's daily wages as a tailor were not enough to make ends meet.

Initially, Gong used the more than one hundred yuan in land rent she had brought from her hometown to Shanghai,

as well as the money she made from selling her clothes and jewelry, to supplement their daily expenses.

Before a year had passed, they were penniless. Shao, unable to maintain the situation, secretly returned to his hometown,

abandoning them in Shanghai. Gong had no choice but to ask

Rong Lu, a fellow villager who worked as a foreman at a yarn factory in Xiaoshadu, to introduce her

to work at the yarn factory. She moved her children to live in the workshop at Caoxiebang, Xiaoshadu.

Soon after, her two daughters also entered the yarn factory to work.

Gong earned more than thirty yuan a month, and in a few years she had saved some money.

Last spring, she returned to her hometown to pay off all the debts

her late husband had owed before his death. She returned to Shanghai to continue working as a female worker. Later, her lover Shao

Xishi discovered that Gong's monthly income was quite high and that she had money in hand. Therefore,

he came to Shanghai a few days ago and went to the workshop in Xiaoshadu, intending to rekindle their old relationship.

However, Gong believed that Shao was ungrateful and had abandoned her when she was in poverty.

She wondered if he still had any conscience and refused to let him stay. Shao harbored resentment in his heart.

Therefore, the next day, while Gong and her daughters were working in the yarn factory,

he lured Lingbao, who was left at home to watch the door, with candy.

He took Lingbao on a tram to the North Railway Station, boarded the

Shanghai-Nanjing Railway, and took Lingbao to his hometown in Wuxi to hide him.

After Lingbao disappeared, Gong reported the incident to the police, but there was no trace of him. Later,

she received a letter from Shao Xishi from Wuxi, stating that Lingbao was now in his hometown and that

she would have to pay one hundred yuan to redeem him. After receiving the letter, Gong traveled to Wuxi overnight by

train and reported the incident to the township office, which rescued Lingbao.

Yesterday, she brought him back to Shanghai by train, and mother and son were reunited. It can be said that it was fortunate.

The Municipal Police Bureau Bans Braids 150

The Shanghai Special City Police Bureau issued a notice yesterday to all district stations

stating: "It has been found that the Ministry of Interior previously issued regulations prohibiting the wearing of braids.

The regulations stipulated that all braids must be cut off within three months of the regulations being posted.

Repeated orders have been issued to strictly investigate and encourage people to cut them off.

However, reports have been received that rickshaw pullers and

ignorant people in the city are still wearing braids and parading in the streets.

It is clear that the district chiefs have not been diligently enforcing the regulations. In addition to forwarding the notice,

you are hereby ordered to instruct your subordinates to investigate at all times

and to instruct the police stationed near the various tax collection offices of the Finance Bureau

to pay attention. If there are people who are wearing braids, they should be taken to the

district station, informed of the benefits and disadvantages, and encouraged to cut them off. They should be dealt with in accordance with Article 6 of the previously

issued regulations on wearing braids, and the situation of compliance

should be reported at any time. This order."

The Problem of Bu Xiao Sheng's Posthumous Works 153

Saying Death Is Not an Insulting Term

Judge Sun Orders Xiang to Appear in Court

The novelist Xiang Kairan (i.e., Bu Xiao Sheng) was previously in litigation with Shihuan Bookstore

over the book "The Head That Flew at Midnight." A judgment was issued the day before yesterday, rejecting Xiang Kairan's claims. Unexpectedly, Xiang recently accused

Dongfang Liang and Jiang Xiahun of the Shanghai Popular Bookstore on Simalu of using a criminal

false identity to deceive readers in the Shanghai Provisional Court.

The reason was that Popular Bookstore published a book called "Guo Ji Da Guan" (National Skills Overview)

with the words "Posthumous Works of Bu Xiao Sheng" added to the top. Therefore, Xiang came out to deny it. Yesterday

afternoon, Judge Sun Yuan presided over the court hearing. The defendants, Dongfang Liang and Jiang

Xiahun, hired lawyer Zhang Chongding, who argued that "Guo Ji Da Guan"

contained articles such as "Thirty-Six Rods in the Mother-Son Style" and "The Great Sword King Wu," which were indeed

written by Xiang Kairan and could be proven with his original manuscript in his own handwriting. Moreover, the manuscript fees

had all been paid, and there was also sufficient evidence. As for the term "posthumous works,"

at the time, there was indeed a rumor in Shanghai that Bu Xiao Sheng had died.

Jing Bao and other newspapers had records of this, which proves that this rumor was not spread by the defendants.

Moreover, everyone must die. Buddhists call it Nirvana, and

Taoists call it ascension. These are by no means insulting terms. Now, on behalf of the defendants,

a counterclaim is being filed against Xiang Kairan, accusing him of fraud and libel.

The judge is requested to order Xiang to appear in court in person. Judge Sun Yuan accepted the testimony.

Since Xiang had not arrived today, the hearing was adjourned to the afternoon of April 10.

At that time, Xiang Kairan must be ordered to appear in court in person.

News of the Nanshi Wharf Being Taken Over 155

The Shanghai Municipal Government Port Authority has reached an agreement with various shipping companies to take back the wharves in South Shanghai

and make them public. Starting in late March, the shipping companies leasing the wharves

will pay a deposit of 700,000 yuan, which will be paid to the Port Authority to

reimburse Da Da and others for the construction costs of the various wharves.

The first installment of the deposit, limited to payment to the Bureau by the end of this month,

is currently facing difficulties for the various Chinese shipping companies in Shanghai to raise

this large sum of money due to the impact of the current situation and financial relations. They have jointly sent a letter to the Port Authority requesting a change in arrangements.

The Municipal Government has issued an instruction stating, in brief, that "According to the financial pressures reported by various shipping merchants,

the deposit can be changed to one-tenth of the original amount to be paid first. The remainder can be paid at a suitable time

when conditions permit. The Port Authority should convene the various shipping merchants to thoroughly discuss the

methods to ensure that the reorganization proceeds smoothly despite the changes." It also ordered that one-tenth of the deposit, which should be paid, be sent to the Finance Bureau,

and the takeover period should be in the middle of next month. In addition, the Ning-Shao and six other companies requested that the Port Authority retain the fee schedule

for berths at each wharf. The reply stated that this case had been approved by the Municipal Government and could not be deleted or changed.

Provisional Court: Oral Examination for Clerks 158

The Special District Local Court will be reorganized and established on April 1 at the original site of the Provisional Court.

Because of the need for clerks, the current president, Xu, has issued a notice to recruit candidates.

After the written examination the day before yesterday, the Examination Committee selected forty

people, including Chen Zhongda, who passed the written examination. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM,

an oral examination was held. Those who applied to the court for the examination arrived on time.

First, the court staff ordered them to gather in the Second Tribunal on the second floor.

A sign with the words "Registration Office" was posted at the entrance of the tribunal. After the forty

people who passed the written examination arrived and their names were checked, the Examination Committee began to call

them into the examination room next to the president's office one by one

for the oral examination. Each person was asked a few questions by the Examination Committee in the examination room

and then left, before the second person was called into the room. The examination was completed at 4:00 PM.

Only those who passed both examinations were qualified to be appointed as clerks. The number of people who will be accepted will be announced soon.

Cook Killed by Car 159

Leading to a Tragic Death

Yin De Kui, a cook in the household of a certain family in Seymour Road, at 7:00 AM the day before yesterday, rode

his bicycle to the small vegetable market to buy vegetables. When he passed Jing'an Temple Road, he turned west.

A car with the number 12077 was traveling in the same direction as Yin, but the car was slightly behind.

Unexpectedly, Yin suddenly turned the wheels of his bicycle and headed north, intending to cross the road,

resulting in a collision with the car that was traveling straight ahead. Yin was seriously injured. A police officer

saw this and sent Yin by car to Baolong Hospital for treatment. He died yesterday morning.

Upon receiving the report, the police ordered an investigation and transported the body to the forensic examination office on Feilun Road.

Subsequently, Judge Ge of the Provisional Court came to the office to verify the cause of death.

He sat in the court and heard testimony from Mr. Talim, a British military officer in the car with the number 12077, who stated that

the car was owned by the Taila Motor Company and that the accident was caused by the dead man's bicycle traveling at excessive speed.

Next, the driver of the car, Wang Linfu, explained the circumstances of the collision at the time.

Yin Zengshi, the dead man's wife, tearfully pleaded for justice. Judge Ge reviewed the testimony and ruled that

the car driver was not at fault and was exempt from prosecution. He also instructed Yin Zengshi to sign a statement and take the body for burial.

He instructed the car company to provide a discretionary amount of compensation to settle the case.

Sixteen Packages of Opium in Sack 160

Yesterday morning at 1:00 AM, Li Chenghua, an inspector of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau's River Patrol Team,

led a team of officers on a patrol along the river on the Bund.

They found a man carrying a sack who appeared flustered.

They immediately conducted an inspection and found sixteen packages of opium in his sack. They immediately took him back to the team.

Captain Xu brought the case for preliminary interrogation. According to his confession, he was named Wu Zhenxing, 24 years old, and was from Wuxi.

He said that the items in the sack were entrusted to him by a friend to be taken to a certain place.

Because the matter involved smuggling opium, he was ordered to prepare a document and submit it

to the Third Section of the Municipal Police Bureau for interrogation.

Rogue Extorts Monk 161

Guangci, a monk, is 27 years old and from Dongtai, Jiangbei. He is currently a guest master at Qinglian Temple on Qinglian Street inside Xiaobeimen.

The day before yesterday (March 21) at about 6:00 PM, a person went to the home of Cui Wu, a fellow villager, at No. 4 Lixing Street for something.

Her husband, Cui Boyi, was out pulling a rickshaw and had not yet returned. Suddenly, five or six rogues grabbed him and forced him to write an IOU for 30 yuan.

At the time, Wang Chengrong, the landlord of the second room, came out to mediate and had Guangci pay 8

yuan in advance, which was handed over to Jiang Xingmao, who lived with him, to be given to the rogues. The next morning, Guangci went to Wang's to return the money.

Yesterday morning, when Guangci went to the same place, Wang and Jiang again demanded money from him. Guangci, in desperation,

grabbed the two of them and took them to the Second Precinct, Second Division, which had jurisdiction over the area.

After a brief interrogation by the chief of the station, a document was prepared and transferred to the Judicial Section for interrogation.

Pacific Union Luncheon Today 162

The Pacific Union will hold a luncheon today at the Cathay Hotel.

Dr. Du Qian, Professor of History and Political Science at Wesleyan University in the United States, will be invited to speak on the topic of "Has Democracy Failed?"

Dr. Du is an expert on speaking for the Far East on behalf of the Carnegie Endowment for International Peace in the United States.

He will lecture at various well-known universities. Currently, he is in Shanghai and will be attending the meeting to speak.

Lost Boy Waiting to be Claimed 163

The Municipal Police Bureau reported yesterday that the Sixth Precinct, First Division, had sent a lost boy named Chen

Fushan, who claimed to be 13 years old and from Dantu. He said that his home was on Gaozi Street and that he had a mother named Chen Chen.

He came to Shanghai on the 22nd day of the first month of the Lunar New Year through the introduction of his fellow villager Zhu Dequan.

He was an apprentice at the Liu Siwu barber shop. He got lost while playing outside. The boy was wearing

a melon-shaped hat, a black cloth cotton robe, black cloth leggings, woolen socks, and black cloth

shoes. The boy has now been sent to the Women and Children's Relief Association to be cared for while waiting to be claimed.

Weather Report 164

The Zikawei Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that

a low-pressure system is moving towards the northeast-east and will reach Jiangsu. Its center has a vortex ring.

There is fog along the coast and rain, or thunderstorms, in the Yangtze River basin. Also,

the highest temperature in the city in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 73.8, and the lowest was 58.0.

On the same day last year, the highest was 55.6 and the lowest was 47.3.

Letter

Sir, I have just read the local news in your newspaper about the Wu Jinwang family being robbed.

The place that was robbed in Dekang Li, Fusheng Road, Zhabei, was the Gonghe Le Sports Association,

not my home. However, I am also a member of the association. Fearing that the rumors are inaccurate,

I would like to request a correction. Wu Jinsheng, 27th of [month unspecified].
