Free Talk

A Chuckle 165

— Haike

Middle-Aged Mother (to her seventy-year-old father*)—Dad, the children are looking for those two dance records. Have you seen them?

Grandfather—Don't make a sound. I'm having fun with them. I'm sitting on them.

A—It's really strange. He's young. Why did he have to marry an old maid?

B—He collects a lot of antiques at home. Marrying an old maid to match makes it feel even more antique.

Housewife—This is really impossible. I can't sleep at night lately. I'm worried about all these bills.

Debt Collector—I'm the same as you. So I have to collect it today. So I don't stay awake again tonight.

Judge—Do you keep committing crimes for the rest of your life? Don't you want to live freely if you keep going to jail?

Criminal—I won't fall for your tricks again. Once I wanted to regain my freedom. I escaped from prison in the middle of the night. Unexpectedly, they caught me. Instead, they extended my prison term by six months.

A Night's Conversation with Dr. Chu 166

— Cailiang

At seven o'clock the night before last, the Chinese Students' Association of the World specially invited Dr. Chu Minyi to give a lecture. The topic was "The Purpose and Method of Physical Education." His exposition was thorough and detailed. Unfortunately, I am forgetful and could not record the main points. I will record a few key points from the speech below to share with those who like to listen to Dr. Chu's lectures.

Promote Domestic Products. Most of the sports equipment currently used are imported goods. As a result, the issue of sports has almost become a patent of the bourgeoisie. Nothing is more unfair than this. For the sake of popularization, it is necessary to promote domestic products. I remember when I was in the National Exhibition, I initiated a shuttlecock kicking competition. At that time, many guests came to participate, so the results were quite good. Unfortunately, the exhibition period was short, so it could not be a permanent exhibition. I hope that people with good intentions will promote it more and make more inventions, so that everyone can achieve the goal of exercise. I can't help but look forward to it.

Recognize the Goal. The common problem of our Chinese people is that they like to talk about the surface. Even in terms of sports, it is no exception. Looking at the results of various Far East competitions in recent years, it is lamentable. This kind of effort to embrace the Buddha's feet when the time is urgent has no hope of success. Moreover, the purpose of physical education is health, and it cannot be achieved overnight. It is meaningless to compete for a moment's length. It is necessary to persist and work hard. Then I dare to say that the loss in the east can be recovered in the evening.

Control Exercise. Confucius said, "Only wine has no limit and is not chaotic." We should also view exercise in the same way. As for today's students in various schools who pay attention to exercise, their enthusiasm is commendable. However, I heard that some people specialize in it and neglect their studies, which seems too much. The time is not economical, and it is also harmful to physiology. The so-called benefit is not seen, but the harm comes first, which is really not worth it. (Repaid)

Record of Mr. Guan's Funeral 167

— Liangyu

Mr. Guan Zhiqing of Wuxi was a pioneer in the business world. He served as the Chinese manager of Siemens for twenty years. He made decisive decisions and spoke clearly. The Germans were usually arrogant, but they were all sincerely convinced by Mr. Guan. If it were not for Mr. Guan's extraordinary talent, how could he have achieved this? Unfortunately, he was troubled by illness last year and suddenly passed away at the end of the year. He loved to give and was generous. Whether they knew him or not, they mourned his death.

The 23rd was the date for the opening of the funeral. On Huanglu Road, the plain cars and white horses blocked the road. There were thousands of mourners, including Wang Zhengting and Yu Qiaqing. The mourning hall, from the corridor to the hall, was full of elegiac couplets and silk banners. The longest eulogy was written by Li Lishan, the host of the Fuxing Temple on Jade Emperor Mountain. The sentence reads, "You are the God of Fortune for the world. Your kindness is widespread. You have been tirelessly giving to the drowning and hungry in your life. Everyone says that good people are blessed by heaven and will surely enjoy a long life. Why did you suddenly suffer from a lingering illness for several years and lack a panacea? You abandoned the mortal world and said goodbye forever. Heaven has taken away my comrade. You passed away in the middle of the road. For ten years, we have supported and helped each other, and protected the Tao with great devotion. We have always admired the profoundness of the Xuan Decree and are determined to cultivate good results. One day, on the Three Life Stone, we will meet old friends again. Do not forget the wind and moon to prove the previous cause." It was written on a ten-foot-long silk, and the characters were also elegant. I also searched my brains and reluctantly composed a couplet: "Solemn Buddha appearance, Bodhisattva heart, happy to cultivate purity and joy, the soul returns to the ethereal and becomes a good fruit.洒脱神情, 金剛氣骨. Expressing beauty in words and deeds, the old generation has lost its model." I am ashamed of my clumsy writing and lack of talent. I am ashamed that I cannot describe Mr. Guan in the slightest.

At 2:30 in the afternoon, the funeral procession departed from Huanglu, passed through North Sichuan Road, and turned into Bazhi Road to Beizhan. There were five places of worship along the way. Mr. Guan believed in Taoism during his lifetime, so there were many Taoist priests, about fifty people. The ceremonial guards stretched for about a mile, extremely winding and slow. Passengers with quick mirrors competed to take pictures. By the time they arrived at Beizhan, it was almost four o'clock. Stationmaster Yuan Shaochang took good care of them and ordered the police to help the filial sons into the rest room for a short rest. Soon, the pallbearers carried the coffin to the scheduled carriage, so that they could be carried back to Wuxi tomorrow morning. With a coffin attached to the body, everything was over. After witnessing this, I could not help but feel sad and sigh. I still remember when I worked at Siemens, I often argued with German women because of my innate arrogance. Mr. Guan always supported me. When I resigned from Siemens and joined McCallie, he repeatedly gave me instructions. From this, I knew that Mr. Guan loved me deeply. Time flies, and life is like a dream. How could I know that Mr. Guan would pass away? I wrote this under the lamp, and I couldn't help but feel sad.

Xiao Shi 168

— Ji Jin

Xunxi Garden is built by a wealthy gentleman named Zhu in the same village. There is a Xiaoshi in the garden, about ten feet high, with a hole in the back, like a mouthful, with a hollow cavity in the middle. When the wind blows, it鳴, and sometimes the sound of呜呜 can be heard. Whenever the狂飈怒發, its sound is even louder. Listening to it in the静夜, it is like a虎嘯山谷, which makes people tremble.

Zhu is obsessed with Yuanzhang. The garden is full of怪石羅列, almost a hundred in number. Among them, some are疊如層巒, and some are悬若峭壁. The shapes are strange and cannot be 殫記. And Xiaoshi is the most. Or云, this stone is 不利. Since 同光, it This is not a complete list, but here is the translation:

Laughable 169

—Hai Ke

A mother in her middle ages (to her seventy-year-old father) – Dad, the children are looking for those two dancing records. Have you seen them?

Grandfather - Don't make a sound. I'm having fun with them. I'm sitting on them.

A—It's really strange. He’s young. Why did he have to marry an old maid?

B—His family has a lot of antique collections. Marrying an old maid to match makes it feel even more antique.

Housewife—This is really impossible. I can't sleep at night lately. It's all because I’m worried about all these bills.

Debt Collector—I am the same as you. So I must collect it today, so I don't stay awake again tonight.

Judge—You're not going to spend your whole life committing crimes and going to jail, are you? Don't you want to live freely?

Criminal—I won't fall for your tricks again. Once, I wanted to regain my freedom. I escaped from prison in the middle of the night. Unexpectedly, they caught me and extended my sentence by six months.

Record of One Evening with Dr. Chu 170

— Cai Liang

At seven o'clock the night before last, the Global Chinese Students' Association specially invited Dr. Chu Minyi to give a lecture. The topic was "The Purpose and Method of Physical Education." He discussed it thoroughly and in detail. Unfortunately, I am forgetful and could not record the main points. I will record a few key points from the speech below to share with those who like to listen to Dr. Chu's lectures.

Promote Domestic Products Most of the sports equipment currently used are imported goods. As a result, the issue of sports has almost become the monopoly of the capitalist class. Nothing is more unfair than this. For the sake of popularization, it is very necessary to promote domestic products. I remember when I was in the National Exhibition, I initiated a shuttlecock kicking competition. At that time, many guests came to participate, so the results were quite good. Unfortunately, the exhibition period was short, so it could not be a permanent exhibition. I hope that people with good intentions will promote it more and make more inventions, so that everyone can achieve the goal of exercise. I can't help but look forward to it.

Recognize the Goal The common problem of our Chinese people is that they like to talk about the surface. Even when it comes to sports, it is no exception. Looking at the results of various Far East competitions in recent years, it is lamentable. This kind of effort to embrace the Buddha's feet when the time is urgent has no hope of success. Moreover, the purpose of physical education is health, and it cannot be achieved overnight. It is meaningless to compete for a moment's length. It is necessary to persevere and work hard. Then I dare to say that what is lost in the east can be recovered in the evening.

Control Exercise Confucius said, "Only wine has no limit and can cause chaos." We should also view exercise in the same way. As for today's students in various schools who pay attention to exercise, their enthusiasm is commendable. However, I heard that some people specialize in it and neglect their studies, which seems too much. The time is not economical, and it is also greatly harmful to physiology. The so-called benefit has not been seen, but the harm comes first, which is really not worth it. (Rewarded)

Record of Mr. Guan's Funeral 171

— Liang Yu

Mr. Guan Zhiqing of Wuxi was a pioneer in the business world. He served as the Chinese manager of Siemens Foreign Firm for twenty years. He made decisive decisions and spoke clearly. The Germans were usually arrogant, but they were all sincerely convinced by Mr. Guan. If it were not for Mr. Guan's extraordinary talent, how could he have achieved this? Unfortunately, he was troubled by illness last year and suddenly passed away at the end of the year. He loved to give and was generous. Whether they knew him or not, they all mourned his death.

The 23rd was the date for the opening of the funeral. On Huanglu Road, the plain cars and white horses blocked the road. There were thousands of mourners, including Wang Zhengting and Yu Qiaqing. The mourning hall, from the corridor to the hall, was full of elegiac couplets and silk banners. The longest eulogy was written by Li Lishan, the host of the Fuxing Temple on Jade Emperor Mountain. The sentence reads, "You are the God of Fortune for the world. Your kindness is widespread. You have been tirelessly giving to the drowning and hungry in your life. Everyone says that good people are blessed by heaven and will surely enjoy a long life. Why did you suddenly suffer from a lingering illness for several years and lack a panacea? You abandoned the mortal world and said goodbye forever. Heaven has taken away my comrade. You passed away in the middle of the road. For ten years, we have supported and helped each other, and protected the Tao with great devotion. We have always admired the profoundness of the Xuan Decree and are determined to cultivate good results. One day, on the Three Life Stone, we will meet old friends again. Do not forget the wind and moon to prove the previous cause." It was written on a ten-foot-long silk, and the characters were also elegant. I also searched my brains and reluctantly composed a couplet: "Solemn Buddha appearance, Bodhisattva heart, happy to cultivate purity and joy, the soul returns to the ethereal and becomes a good fruit.洒脱神情, 金剛氣骨. Expressing beauty in words and deeds, the old generation has lost its model." I am ashamed of my clumsy writing and lack of talent. I am ashamed that I cannot describe Mr. Guan in the slightest.

At 2:30 in the afternoon, the funeral procession departed from Huanglu, passed through North Sichuan Road, and turned into Bazhi Road to Beizhan. There were five places of worship along the way. Mr. Guan believed in Taoism during his lifetime, so there were many Taoist priests, about fifty people. The ceremonial guards stretched for about a mile, extremely winding and slow. Passengers with quick mirrors competed to take pictures. By the time they arrived at Beizhan, it was almost four o'clock. Stationmaster Yuan Shaochang took good care of them and ordered the filial sons into the rest room for a short rest. Soon, the pallbearers carried the coffin to the scheduled carriage, so that they could be carried back to Wuxi tomorrow morning. With a coffin attached to the body, everything was over. After witnessing this, I could not help but feel sad and sigh. I still remember when I worked at Siemens, I often argued with German women because of my innate arrogance. Mr. Guan always supported me. When I resigned from Siemens and joined McCallie, he repeatedly gave me instructions. From this, I knew that Mr. Guan loved me deeply. Time flies, and life is like a dream. How could I know that Mr. Guan would pass away? I wrote this under the lamp, and I couldn't help but feel sad.

Howling Stone 172

— Ji Jin

Xunxi Garden is built by a wealthy gentleman named Zhu in the same village. There is a Howling Stone in the garden, about ten feet high, with a hole in the back, like a mouthful, with a hollow cavity in the middle. When the wind blows, it makes a sound, and sometimes the sound of woo-woo can be heard. Whenever there is a狂飈怒發, its sound is even louder. Listening to it in the quiet night, it is like a tiger howling in the valley, which makes people tremble.

Zhu is obsessed with Yuanzhang. The garden is full of strange stones, almost a hundred in number. Among them, some are stacked like layers of mountains, and some are suspended like cliffs. The shapes are strange and cannot be described in detail. And Xiaoshi is the most. Some say that this stone is unlucky. Since Tongguang, it has changed owners ten times. Mr. Zhu did not believe it and bought it for a thousand gold. Before long, the owner died and the family business declined. And the survival of this stone is not yet known. So, in the darkness, there is also a number for things and people. I am afraid it cannot be borrowed. I will record it to express my remote sigh.

News of Fishing and Hunting 173

— Lonely Xu Sheng

A guest talked about fishing and hunting, which was quite novel and delightful. I recorded it to help with conversation. The coastal area of ​​eastern Zhejiang has a special product: wild ducks. They have flat beaks and brown feathers, and they fly in groups. They gather especially in fields and beaches because they eat barnyard millet. Hunters often tie grass into the shape of a human and insert it into the field. At first, the wild ducks are suspicious and afraid, and they all fly away. After a long time, they know it is harmless and no longer pay attention to it. Then, the hunters mix croton powder with grains and spread them on the field. Then, they hide among the grass bundles. After a while, the wild ducks gather and compete to peck at the grains. When the croton poison takes effect, the wild ducks all tremble and fall down one after another, unable to fly away. The hunters rush out and catch them, filling their bags without any effort. As the saying goes, "People die for wealth, and birds die for food." It is true.

Everyone knows that fishing is done with nets or hooks. However, the people of Yongbo are quite skilled at catching fish. The fisherman rolls flour into bait and sticks it to both ends of a bamboo silk. Each bamboo silk is tied to a line and suspended in a bamboo pole. There are probably hundreds of baits. They sink it into the water. After a long time, the fish come to swallow the bait. When the bait enters the mouth, the bamboo silk springs open and just holds the fish's mouth. It cannot escape. The fisherman raises the bamboo pole, and the fish are all suspended below it, as if they were being caught. He gets a lot of fish. It can be said that he is ingenious. I have heard that torches are used to catch crabs, and frog legs are used to hook frogs. Creatures that fly and crawl are ignorant and deserve to be caught. However, apes are primates, and they are also deceived by humans. It is said that there are many apes in Tiantai Mountain. They often come in groups in the bamboo forests and take wild fruits and bamboo shoots as usual. Therefore, the villagers plant trees in the mountains, wrapping them with bamboo shoots, so they look like bamboo shoots. When the monkeys come, one monkey will often stand upright on the bamboo shoot, and another monkey will tie it with a rope, pretending to break off the bamboo shoot. Then, they carry it away. The villagers use their intelligence. The monkeys initially do not know. When they are tied up and the bamboo shoot is not broken, the villagers come out and catch them, as easy as turning their hands. Alas. Human intelligence is above that of animals, so it is natural for animals to fail. However, human intelligence varies greatly. I

Foreign Rice Prices Soar Unabated 184

Spot goods up two to three jiao... Futures also up

Yesterday, because domestic customers were competing to purchase and the arrival of goods was not sustained, foreign rice prices continued to increase.

Spot goods in the market were very scarce. The sellers who opened yesterday were all return goods, so they rose two to three jiao compared to the previous market.

Spot goods are scarce and goods in transit are tight. Goods arriving tomorrow and the day after and goods delivered around April 2-3 all rose by about two jiao, but

the goods arriving recently had already been sold in advance, with spot goods totaling less than 10,000 bags.

There were only 8,000 bags of small-grain brown rice spot goods, priced at 12.85 yuan, which was still enough for domestic customers.

Number 1 Saigon opened to 15.45 yuan, and Mindang opened to 15.1 yuan. Number 1 goods in transit were the same as spot goods, and number 2 goods in transit were 14.8 yuan. Large-grain goods in transit were 14.15 yuan.

Although Tongxingtai and Haiyangshe sold 10,000 tons of large and small grains in futures, because domestic and interior customers were competing to purchase, the market price jumped by almost 1 qian.

The return goods totaled 1,800 tons, and the market was 2-3 fen better than the foreign firms' selling prices.

The Tapioca Market is Gradually Improving, Especially in the Far Term 185

Spot Sales are Weak

Yesterday, after the tapioca market opened in the morning, the trend for each month remained positive. Because

foreign wheat reported good prices of 2-3-4 jiao, the current increases and decreases seemed to be purely controlled by the large

bulls. If there was a slight release, the market conditions would immediately loosen. Otherwise, there was a

trend of continuous increases. Regarding the actual situation, although factories' stocks were not very

large, Tianjin's attitude was indifferent, because this kind of market value could not be calculated.

There was very little possibility of purchasing, so although the standards were good, spot sales had turned weak.

When the afternoon market opened, the current month's trend showed signs of fluctuation. In April and May, large bull

customers had slightly reduced their positions, and large short customers had also covered their positions.

The market mood was slightly soft, but then the bulls gained strength again and tended to be firm and high. New flour in the far term had very strong purchasing enthusiasm outside the industry. Factories were not selling, and the market was exceptionally profitable. Considering

the current state, the near and far terms will likely continue to improve. As a

result, the current month was unchanged compared to the previous day, April was up by 5 li, May-July

were up by 1 fen and 2.5 li each, and August was up by 7.5 li.

Wheat for Delivery Soars by Six Fen 186

Spot goods opened for 13,000 bags

Yesterday, after the opening of the futures wheat market in the morning and afternoon, each month continued to increase sharply.

The opening price for the current month in the morning was still considered fair, but in the afternoon, because there were still a small number of short positions that needed to be covered, the opening price was raised by 4 fen, and then it remained firm.

The total amount of deliveries was 60 truckloads, of which local factories accounted for 70-80%, and the remainder was collected by traders.

The new crop in the far term had a very bullish market mood because rice prices were increasing day by day.

Buyers in the interior were still continuing to absorb, so the price was also raised step by step. As a result, the

current month suddenly increased by 6 fen compared to the previous day, April increased by 4 fen, and June-August

increased by 3 fen each. The spot market conditions were very good for the factories. The entire market opened for 10,000

and 3,000 bags, opening for Suzhou wheat, Guandian wheat, Qingjiangpu wheat at 5 taels, 1 qian,

1 fen, Jiangxi wheat at 4 taels, 6 qian, 8 fen, Xianghe wheat at 4 taels, 7 qian,

Hankou wheat at 4 taels, 8 qian, 7 fen, 4 taels, 7 qian, 5 fen, 4 taels, 5 qian, 7

fen, 4 taels, 5 qian, 2 fen, 4 taels, 3 qian, 2 fen, which was purchased by Fufeng, Shenda,

and other factories.

Silk and Tea: Before the Inspection Period, Chinese Silk Sales Were Busy 187

Foreign Firms are Urgently Pressing for Delivery... To be Shipped Before April 1

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau scheduled to inspect exported Chinese silk, but because the manufacturers

were unprepared, the deadline was extended to April 1. Before the deadline, the bureau would issue an exemption certificate for inspection and release with customs approval. It is now known that the April 1 deadline for silk inspection by European firms has arrived. In addition to

shipping out the silks stored in foreign warehouses in batches, they are now sending letters to each Chinese silk merchant who has agreed to sell futures silk, asking them to deliver the

futures silk for this month in advance, so that they can be shipped out before the inspection period.

As a result, in recent days, Chinese merchants who have agreed to sell futures silk have been busy delivering to foreign firms, weighing and

packaging, and the overseas silk cable to Shanghai has also been strong. Because Chinese merchants are holding firm on their costs, the prices have turned from firm to increased. Yesterday, Lianna and others purchased 80 bales of white silk, and Qianli purchased 40 bales of grey silk, and the prices have all risen sharply by 5 taels.

New Information on Xiuwu Black Tea 188

The black tea produced in Xiushui, Wuning, Tonggu, and other counties is a major export from Jiangxi Province.

In recent years, both the production volume and sales market have increased compared to previous years. Merchants traveling to the mountains to purchase tea have also become increasingly prevalent. Last year, tea firms in the Xiuwu area, including those from Anhui, Guangdong, and locally based groups, totaled more than thirty. The cost of mountain tea is not as high as that of Keemun tea, and the market shows signs of recovery. However, due to the impact of the suspended operations of the Sino-Russian Association in transit, sales to Russia have come to a standstill. Demand from England and France has decreased, and the lower prices have resulted in significant losses for most tea firms. This year, although new tea is about to enter the market, only about a dozen firms from Anhui, Guangdong, and local groups are preparing to enter the mountains for processing. The rest are adopting a wait-and-see approach, and many are temporary in nature. If the situation stabilizes in the future and finances become more accessible, it is possible that new firms may join. According to tea farmers in the Xiuwu mountains, the tea trees were also damaged by the cold and snow pressure last winter, causing frostbite to the branches. With the Qingming Festival approaching, although tea buds are emerging, they are not as lush and vigorous as in previous years. It is predicted that this year's output will definitely be reduced compared to previous years.

Qing Feng Yuan Di (A Land of Greenery)

The Ongoing Book Collection Campaign at Great China University 190

Great China University, which has been established for more than seven years, has always had a strong atmosphere of teacher-student cooperation. Its excellent achievements today can largely be attributed to the nurturing of this atmosphere. Recently, a so-called book collection campaign has been launched, which is another manifestation of teacher-student cooperation.

Originally, the university's library was not fully equipped, and the books it contained were not sufficient for the students' needs. Although each student had to pay two yuan for library fees per semester, and professors also occasionally donated books, it was ultimately limited. Therefore, when the university applied for registration last year, the Ministry of Education expressed deep dissatisfaction with this point and encouraged efforts to improve it. Now, the ongoing book collection campaign seems to be making some progress in this regard. This campaign was planned by the university's Library Committee and is scheduled to run from April 21st to May 4th. The collection method is as follows: each student is required to collect at least three Chinese books, each worth more than three yuan, or at least five English books, each worth more than one yuan. Those who do not have books will pay a substitute fee of five yuan. Professors are required to collect at least three Chinese books, each worth more than six yuan, or at least five English books, each worth more than two yuan. Those who do not have books will pay a substitute fee of ten yuan. There are also corresponding measures for alumni. In addition to the above collection methods, there are also incentive measures. In the future, the first-place winner with the most books collected individually will be awarded a silver shield by the university, and the group with the most books will be given a velvet banner to show encouragement. It is predicted that this campaign will achieve remarkable results. (Shi Duo)

The location has been changed to the upper floor of the Paris Grand Theatre on Avenue Joffre.

The Nanguo Art Society's regular exhibition was mentioned in yesterday's newspaper. The original address was the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association on Xizang Road in this city. However, due to unresolved negotiations, the society has borrowed the coffee room on the upper floor of the Paris Grand Theatre (west end of Hualong Road) on Avenue Joffre. The location is suitable, and there are many exhibits. The exhibition will be open for three days from today (the 28th) at noon until the 30th of this month. All are welcome to visit.

The Preparatory Course Issue at Jiaotong University 193

Since its reorganization in 1927, Jiaotong University has focused on abolishing primary and secondary schools and concentrating on developing the university itself. After the persistent appeals of students' parents in primary and secondary schools, the high school department was changed to a preparatory course, and the junior high and primary schools were changed to the private Nanyang Model Primary and Secondary School. Graduates could still be promoted, but only until 1932. The establishment of the preparatory course at the school was not originally intended. The Ministry of Education recently issued a notice ordering all universities to abolish preparatory courses. After receiving the order, Jiaotong University held a school affairs meeting and resolved to stop admitting new students to the preparatory first year starting this semester. However, due to the contract with Nanyang Primary and Secondary School, graduates of Nanyang can still be promoted to the preparatory first year, but no new students will be recruited. After the contract expires in 1932, the preparatory course will be gradually abolished, and by 1935, there will be no preparatory course at all. The school also noted that the academic level of students from outside is generally poor. If the first year of the undergraduate program recruits students, it will be very difficult. Therefore, it is proposed to extend the university by one year, and applicants must be high school graduates and study for one more year, which is actually a disguised preparatory course. (Quan)

Social News

Urban Sketches by Lin 200

(7) A Trip Along the Suzhou Creek

Shanghai's waterways, apart from the Huangpu River, are second only to the Suzhou Creek. There are many wharves along the river. Travelers coming to Shanghai from the Su (Suzhou), Chang (Changzhou), and inland river areas mostly disembark at the wharves of Tianhou Temple Bridge and Pentang Lane Bridge. Every morning at eight or nine o'clock, before the small ferries depart, many old and young, men and women, crowd the wharves. Soon, the whistle blows a few times, and wisps of black smoke billow from the chimneys onto the shore. The small ferries gradually leave the riverbank and head west, towing seven or eight boats of various sizes behind them, connected end to end, resembling a long snake winding its way along. This is a very common sight on the Suzhou Creek. When we read in the newspaper about bandits robbing ferries on the lake, we are reminded of the impressions we get on the banks of the Suzhou Creek.

Compared to the Huangpu River, the Suzhou Creek is naturally far inferior. The Huangpu River is like a large courtyard of a house, with its doors wide open, delighting those who see it. The Suzhou Creek is not like that; it is more like an alley behind the kitchen, not only cramped in its location, but also with everything carrying a dirty appearance. Therefore, along the Huangpu River, there are many people strolling with their hands behind their backs, gazing at the river view, while the situation along the Suzhou Creek is very different. In the section between Waibaidu Bridge and Tianhou Temple Bridge, there are still some places where one can linger and appreciate. However, the further west one goes, the more different it becomes. When one reaches the area of Tanziwan and Xiaoshadu, it feels like leaving the city altogether, with a desolate and bleak atmosphere pervading both banks. Especially the section near Guangzhao Villa, where the population is sparse, is like being neighbors with the land of ghosts.

The scenery along the banks of the river can be divided into three different periods. If we use the bridges spanning the river as a standard, then the section west of Waibaidu Bridge and east of Tianhou Temple Bridge is like a young person, full of vigor and joy, with the architecture and scenery on both banks exuding neatness and splendor everywhere. The section between Tianhou Temple Bridge and the sampan factory bridge at the end of Maigen Road is the most complex and bustling, with the most boats in the river. This tedious and endless situation is like a person in middle age, desperately trying to solve their life's problems. As for the sampan factory bridge, it is the last bridge on both banks of the Suzhou Creek. West of it, there are no more bridges, and crossing the river requires a ferry. The scenery on both banks becomes increasingly desolate, like an old person whose vitality is diminishing. In the area of Tanziwan and Xiaoshadu, many people from Jiangbei live on small boats, but these boats never float in the water. Instead, they are called upon to leave the water, land, and live by the shore. These lifeless boats can well represent the general situation of this section of the Suzhou Creek.

The first section of the Suzhou Creek includes Waibaidu Bridge, Libaidu Bridge, Sichuan Road Bridge, Jiangxi Road Bridge, and Tianhou Temple Bridge (Henan Road Bridge). The "Bai" character in Waibaidu Bridge is probably a misprint of the character "Bai" (擺), meaning to set up or arrange. That place also has a name called "Touba" (頭壩, first dam). What was the scenery of the Suzhou Creek like decades ago? These two characters can tell us something about it. Standing on the bridge and looking east, the water of the Huangpu River flows into the Suzhou Creek right under your feet. To the south is the Bund Park, a corner that forms a wall where the two waters meet. Waibaidu Bridge is also called "Huayuan Bridge" (花園橋, Garden Bridge) in the west, and the Bund Park is indeed very closely related to it. There is indeed a garden dedicated to growing flowers under the bridge, which can be seen at a glance from the bridge. Among them, a glass greenhouse is exceptionally quiet. Against the wall is a self-flowing spring, with water flowing from above into the pool, the green shadows reflected on it, making the interior even more serene.

Looking west from the bridge, the nearest is the Erbaidu Bridge. Both banks of the Erbaidu Bridge also have "leisurely and elegant" decorations. On the south side of the riverbank, there are often yachts burning gasoline, staying on the river. The inside of the boats is cleaned like a hospital. The old boatmen also show a sense of self-respect. Except when their masters go out for a tour, they follow along. On weekdays, they clean and scrub the boat all day long, so that dirt and dust are completely avoided. Among the boats entering and exiting the Suzhou Creek, some carry passengers and some tow cargo. Nine out of ten boats are bloated, only the yachts are slender, with well-proportioned bodies, like the ladies of the Suzhou Creek.

Between Baidu Bridge and Sichuan Road Bridge, there are churches, hospitals, hotels, cinemas, and flower shops along the banks. Especially near Libaidu Bridge on the south bank, the roads are flat, and the scenery is quiet and secluded. When the sun is about to set, the river breeze blows from the east, caressing people's faces, no less pleasant than strolling along the riverbank. The post office at the northern end of Sichuan Road Bridge is the only important building on the banks of the Suzhou Creek. The commercial council of Tianhou Temple Bridge also has its due position. When Tianhou Temple was reorganized, there were many vendors and astrologers inside. There are also many people who come to worship the gods. Besides the City God Temple and the Red Temple, Tianhou Temple can also be counted as the third most important place. Now, the front door is deserted, not as good as before. This is also a change related to the banks of the Suzhou Creek.

Looking at the vehicles and pedestrians passing by the bridge, the scene is almost a unique feature of the banks of the Suzhou Creek. There is an iron frame on the Waibaidu Bridge, crisscrossing and arching high above the bridge surface. At night, when the tram passes over the bridge, looking from afar, the lights in the carriages shine through the gaps, which is very interesting. At night on the banks of the Suzhou Creek, you can also see the spires of the three department stores, towering in the air. Looking back to the east, although there are tall buildings behind, the lights on the boats are reflected in the water, rippling and swaying. The air on both banks seems to be much quieter, but a motorcycle quickly drives across the bridge, and the silent air undulates like the river again.

Eunuch Sanbao in Nanyang by YS 201

(10) Sanbao Cave

This was Eunuch Sanbao's seventh voyage, and it was also his last trip to Nanyang. At that time, it was 1433. He and his more than 20,000 soldiers and civilians sailed to Nanyang on dozens of "big-eyed chicken" ships.

Once, as these dozens of "big-eyed chicken" ships were sailing smoothly, for some reason, a monstrous wave suddenly arose, and the wind began to howl. These dozens of "big-eyed chicken" ships swayed like cradles, drifting in the vast ocean.

At this time, the soldiers and civilians on these dozens of "big-eyed chicken" ships were all vomiting. They vomited so severely that they naturally had no strength left. At this time, even the virtuous Eunuch Sanbao could not think of any remedy. This group of vomiting, pitiful soldiers and civilians could only lie down in the cradle-like "big-eyed chicken" ships, "resigned to fate."

Soon, the waves gradually grew larger, and the wind gradually became stronger. At this time, the swaying of the ships became even more violent. The mountain-overturning, sea-swallowing swaying made that group of vomiting soldiers and civilians even more intensely unbearable.

At this time, Eunuch Sanbao himself began to vomit. He could not think of any way to remedy the situation. The thought of "resigning to fate" may have been floating in his mind at this time. So, other than lying down, everything else seemed to be of no concern to him.

The wind and waves grew stronger day by day. This was already the third day, and the waves still showed no signs of calming down.

The wind and waves on the fourth day were even more fierce. These dozens of "big-eyed chicken" ships were originally sailing together, but at this time, they had already been scattered by the wind and waves. However, those pitiful soldiers and civilians lying in the "big-eyed chicken" ships were still unaware of this.

On the fifth day, Eunuch Sanbao could not bear this suffering any longer, so he began to curse.

"If I still have to suffer such great wind and waves, I would rather die quickly!" As soon as he finished speaking, a huge wave overturned his lone ship. As a result, the people on board were completely drowned, and the ship slowly sank to the bottom of the sea.

Just as Eunuch Sanbao's ship sank, the wind and waves stopped the next day. Who knew that not far from the site where Eunuch Sanbao's ship sank, there were small, desolate islands?

Time flashed like lightning. A month quickly passed. At this time, in a remote part of that desolate island, a cave emerged. From a distance, that cave looked like an overturned ship. The cave was full of strange trees. Those trees hung down in a messy way, like iron chains. This cave, it is said, was Eunuch Sanbao's ship. Later, for some reason, this legend of Sanbao Cave spread among the people in the south.

Dr. De Succeeds in Treating Diseases with Gold 202

Cures Patients with Arteriosclerosis

According to German reports, Dr. Schtanfiel of Germany has recently used gold preparations for injections to cure patients with arteriosclerosis, which has attracted much attention in the medical community. The doctor first experimented with mice in the research room of the University of Hamburg, and then tried intravenous and subcutaneous injections on about 20 patients, all of which were quickly successful. Among the gold preparations, "Thai Er Genaier" has the best results, because gold has the property of dilating capillaries and also stimulates spherical cell tissues, which is also related to the secretion of secretions, so it is effective for arteriosclerosis.

The Employment Problem of Jiaotong University Graduates Can Be Solved 204

In China today, where there are more people than jobs, university graduates who have received higher education are unemployed and have nothing to do. Therefore, the general public does not trust the school system, thinking that schools are not places for cultivating talents, unlike the imperial examination system in the past, where scholars could easily dedicate themselves to the country and do something earth-shattering. This view is indeed correct, and students generally feel that studying is boring, and their grades are therefore poor. The reason why education in our country cannot be improved is probably because of this. Jiaotong University in this city is directly under the Ministry of Railways, has a history of 30 years, and its reputation has long been spread throughout China. It is divided into four colleges: Electrical Engineering, Mechanical Engineering, Civil Engineering, and Transportation Management. These four colleges are all directly related to the transportation industry. The cultivation of railway transportation talents completely depends on the school, so the responsibility it bears is indeed not small. In the past, although there were regulations for graduates to be sent to various railways for internships by the Ministry, the standards for appointment after the internship were not regulated. Therefore, many interns were treated harshly by railway staff, and were unable to be promoted to formal positions after the internship, resulting in unemployment. Since last year, the vice president of the school has been held concurrently by Li Zhaohuan, the vice minister of railways. Li is enthusiastic about education and believes that the lack of regulations to guarantee the appointment of graduates is sufficient to affect the students' performance at school. Therefore, he proposed at the ministerial meeting to formulate the "Regulations for the Registration, Appointment, and Guarantee of Jiaotong University Graduates," which has been passed and will be implemented soon. From now on, Jiaotong University students will not have to worry about unemployment, and they will be promoted grade by grade, with rules to guarantee their positions. The important points of the regulations are listed below: (1) All graduates of Jiaotong University directly under the Ministry of Railways who have interned on various railways for one year will be promoted to formal technicians, and their rank will be classified as fifth grade fourth class to first class (see attached table below). (2) Technicians who have been registered and appointed by various railways shall not be dismissed from their positions unless due to negligence. (3) If any railway dismisses a technician without cause, the technician may request the director in writing to state the reasons. If a formal reply is not received, a request should be submitted to the Ministry of Railways for verification and decision. (4) Technicians of various railways who have achieved excellent results for more than one year may be promoted by one grade.

Attached Table of Technical Personnel Salary and Rank Responsibilities

First grade first class 700, second class 600, third class 550, fourth class 500 (Director of Engineering Bureau). Second grade first class 450, second class 400, third class 360, fourth class 320 (Chief Engineer or Director). Third grade first class 300, second class 285, third class 270, fourth class 255 (Engineers or Assistant Engineers). Fourth grade first class 340, second class 320, third class 200, fourth class 280 (Construction Workers). Fifth grade first class 240, second class 220, third class 100, fourth class 80 (Construction Workers). (Quan)

Art World

The Metropolitan Nature of Modern Art by Zhang Ruogu 207

In the March issue of the Japanese magazine "New Tide," there is a review by Mr. Niikyo entitled "The Metropolitan Nature of Modern Art." The main idea of ​​that paper is to explain that urban literature and art have become the main elements of modern art. The author first cites the phenomenon that film art tends to portray urban life, such as tall buildings, street scenes, crowds of pedestrians, and transportation organizations, all of which have become indispensable urban portrayal backgrounds for modern films.

The great film "Berlin Metropolis Symphony" and other films depicting the lives of New York or Paris have been warmly welcomed by people in major cities around the world.

All literary and artistic works that take urban life as the central expression can give modern people considerable seduction and satisfaction. Many colorful entertainment organizations in cities, such as theaters, cinemas, concert halls, dance halls, amusement parks, hotels, sports fields, swimming pools, etc., have been regarded by general writers as excellent themes for movies, paintings, or popular novels. "Urban life," "urban enjoyment," "urban color," "urban feeling," "urban love," "urban melancholy," "urban literature," "urban art"... a long string of new terms has also emerged accordingly.

Mr. Niikyo also discusses the opposition and comparative distinction between urban literature and peasant literature. The rapid pace of urban nature, the scientific clarity and convenience, the expansion of new sensations, moderate enjoyment, trial marriages, and the various issues of marriage bankruptcy are exquisitely reasoned. Limited to space, it is impossible to translate and list them in detail here, for which I am deeply sorry.

Recently, in the Japanese literary and art circles, a great wave of literary and artistic inclination towards urbanism has been set off. It is expected that this emerging literature and art will soon emerge in the Japanese literary and art world, which is an inevitable fact.

The late, famous Japanese critic, Mr. Katagami Shin, wrote an essay entitled "Urban Life and Modern Literature." He affirmed that the most humane thing in human life is urban life, and the most intense desires in life also exist in urban life. Therefore, in a sense, urban life is a symbol of human life. To admire urban life is to be passionately in love with the most intense human life.

Urban life is always the activity center of a country, a nation, or an international nation. Therefore, in all aspects, there must be the light of life actively moving there. Urban life has acute moods, but lacks the taste of slowness and leisure, and it is also the most stimulating. It is just like the sun at noon, with light, heat, and the liveliness of color, but on the other hand, it is inevitable that there is a kind of rotten and decadent shadow, and a dark image covered with fatigue and weariness.

Since urban life has its beautiful, rich, and bright advantages, it also naturally has ugly, monotonous, and dark places. Therefore, some people praise urban life, while others curse urban life.

The literature and art produced in urban areas are those that exaggerate the subtlety and acuteness of the senses and regard the strong stimulation and graceful emotions as life. The characteristic and value of so-called urban art is that even in the decline of the senses or the fatigue of the spirit, there is still a kind of "demand for life," and even in the sigh of failure, there is still a strong desire and love for life.

Those who curse urban life and urban art are definitely not because their bodies and minds are exhausted, but because their hearts for loving life and admiring the world have long withered. At the same time, they have lost that sense of wonder and mystery about their own lives. We cannot but express considerable grief for their great loss.

Recent art, such as futurism and expressionism, expresses that kind of turbulent, uneasy, and stimulating urban sentiment. It uses trams, cars, moving pictures, and licentious demons to replace those fields, villages, water surfaces, sail shadows, and pure virgins as the themes of paintings. A group of artists all jumped out of the mountains and rivers and gathered in the metropolis...

The places of entertainment in the metropolis are extremely complex. These many places of entertainment can make you taste endless fun and get infinite inspiration. If you sit in a coffee shop, you will definitely meet that seventeen or eighteen-year-old virgin, and under the red lights and green wine, she will carefully recount her past romance to you...

In the Japanese literary world, there have recently been so-called new sensory writers. Their creations are all newly created based on modern Japanese urban life. Mr. Liu Na'ou has selected and translated them into a collection entitled "Erotic Culture." Each article is very sharp and lively and lovely. Among them, Yokomitsu Riichi's "The Seventh Floor Exercise" and Iketani Shinzaburo's "Bridge" are the most beautiful.

Mr. Liu Na'ou was also the first to introduce Paul Morand ABC, the leading writer of modern French urban literature, to China (there is Mr. Dai Wangshu's selected translation collection "Celestial Jade Beauty"). What Morand has achieved in his literary efforts is the new method of writing, the new form of speech, the new tone, the reform of foreign-flavored writing, and the renewal of custom research, a method that makes people laugh and smile. Although the devious twists and turns of his articles are a bit too novel and too numerous, they are actually very interesting and will not cause any disgust. The painting characteristics of Morand's articles and the clever composition method of color and line are worthy of our detailed research.

Since Mr. Liu Na'ou so highly respects French and Japanese new sensory writers, in his own creations, such as "Two People at Different Times," "Game," and "Program," etc., are all very impressive works, each filled with a strong urban color and a very sharp urban feeling.

In my personal opinion, in addition to loving the passionate works of French Romantic writers of the 19th century, I am also quite interested in the works of the above-mentioned new sensory writers.

But rather than saying that I admire the content of the new sensory works, I would rather say that I admire their form and style. Although Morand's novels are good at expressing the pain of human nature in urban life, I am very dissatisfied with the cold, ridiculing attitude that lacks sympathy. I only love his skillful style, his strokes are very fresh and lovely, it is a film-like flash method, the summary order method of emotional analysis, the abbreviation method, the separation method, and the listing method. His collection skills of sporadic characters can only be used by clever and clever artists, but if we look at the nature and content of the works, Morand's works cannot be included in the ranks of world-class writers. The fragment about the photography of department stores in Iketani Saburo's "Bridge" is also unusually lively and lovely, and the artistic quality of that "Bridge" is also quite outstanding, but it is not that I want to erase the Japanese writers, I always feel that Liu Na'ou's works are much more lovely, because in Na'ou's several works, not only are the technical aspects very delicate and precise, but what I admire most is that he does not have a cold attitude. His works are not only rich in the color of oriental cities and thicker than the atmosphere of the oriental world, but also have a tolerant temperament unique to the Chinese nation, which is far beyond the reach of the trivialities of the Japanese nation and the satire of the French nation.

Editor's Note: The tendency of modern art to be metropolitan is just in its ascendant. This article by the author is only a narrative of its general outline. However, Chinese old artists have not felt this trend at all. At a recent exhibition of a certain country's paintings, there seemed to be a few such declarations: "The spring is bright and the scenery is pleasant. At the head of the Huangpu River, everything that catches the eye is a field of sound, color, goods, and profits, with very few places of noble entertainment. Therefore, we gather this meeting to send away elegant interests," etc. This is really starting from nowhere.

The "Art World" on the 24th of this month contained the entry "The first collection of hidden essentials has been published in four types" was mistakenly inserted. This is hereby corrected.
